## Part 3: Polymorphic State Model, AI Role Enforcement & Stack Selector

---

### §2.1 Polymorphic State Model

#### §2.1.1 Core Enumerations

```python
from enum import Enum

class Stage(str, Enum):
    S0_INTAKE     = "S0_INTAKE"
    S1_LEGAL      = "S1_LEGAL"
    S2_BLUEPRINT  = "S2_BLUEPRINT"
    S3_CODEGEN    = "S3_CODEGEN"
    S4_BUILD      = "S4_BUILD"
    S5_TEST       = "S5_TEST"
    S6_DEPLOY     = "S6_DEPLOY"
    S7_VERIFY     = "S7_VERIFY"
    S8_HANDOFF    = "S8_HANDOFF"
    COMPLETED     = "COMPLETED"     # Terminal success — project finished all stages
    HALTED        = "HALTED"        # Terminal failure — requires manual intervention

class TechStack(str, Enum):
    FLUTTERFLOW    = "flutterflow"
    REACT_NATIVE   = "react_native"
    SWIFT          = "swift"
    KOTLIN         = "kotlin"
    UNITY          = "unity"
    PYTHON_BACKEND = "python_backend"

class ExecutionMode(str, Enum):
    CLOUD  = "cloud"
    LOCAL  = "local"
    HYBRID = "hybrid"

class AutonomyMode(str, Enum):
    AUTOPILOT = "autopilot"
    COPILOT   = "copilot"

class AIRole(str, Enum):
    SCOUT      = "scout"       # Perplexity Sonar — READ-ONLY research
    STRATEGIST = "strategist"  # Claude Opus 4.6 — planning, legal, War Room
    ENGINEER   = "engineer"    # Claude Sonnet 4.5 — code, files, fixes
    QUICK_FIX  = "quick_fix"   # Claude Haiku 4.5 — syntax, validation
```

#### §2.1.2 Valid Stage Transitions

```python
VALID_TRANSITIONS: dict[Stage, list[Stage]] = {
    Stage.S0_INTAKE:    [Stage.S1_LEGAL,     Stage.HALTED],
    Stage.S1_LEGAL:     [Stage.S2_BLUEPRINT, Stage.HALTED],
    Stage.S2_BLUEPRINT: [Stage.S3_CODEGEN,   Stage.HALTED],
    Stage.S3_CODEGEN:   [Stage.S4_BUILD,     Stage.HALTED],
    Stage.S4_BUILD:     [Stage.S5_TEST,      Stage.HALTED],
    Stage.S5_TEST:      [Stage.S6_DEPLOY, Stage.S3_CODEGEN, Stage.HALTED],  # S3 = fix loop
    Stage.S6_DEPLOY:    [Stage.S7_VERIFY,    Stage.HALTED],
    Stage.S7_VERIFY:    [Stage.S8_HANDOFF, Stage.S6_DEPLOY, Stage.HALTED],  # S6 = redeploy
    Stage.S8_HANDOFF:   [Stage.COMPLETED,    Stage.HALTED],
    Stage.COMPLETED:    [],  # Terminal success — no outbound transitions
    Stage.HALTED:       [],  # Terminal failure — requires manual intervention
}
```

**Stage Semantics:**

| State | Type | Meaning | Recovery |
|-------|------|---------|----------|
| S0–S8 | Active | Project is in progress at this stage | Stuck detection resumes from last snapshot |
| COMPLETED | Terminal (success) | All stages finished; project handed off to operator | No action needed; excluded from stuck detection |
| HALTED | Terminal (failure) | Stopped due to error, budget, legal, or operator action | Manual intervention via Telegram; operator can `/restore` and retry |

**Continuous Legal Thread** does not appear as a stage transition — it runs as a parallel coroutine alongside each stage (see §2.7.3). It can inject a HALT from any stage by setting `state.legal_halt = True` with a reason.

#### §2.1.3 PipelineState (Polymorphic)

The state model is stack-agnostic. It uses a polymorphic `project_metadata` that stores stack-specific data as typed JSON, validated by stack-specific Pydantic models at S2.

```python
from pydantic import BaseModel, Field, model_validator, field_validator
from typing import Optional, Any
from datetime import datetime, timezone

# All collection-type fields use Field(default_factory=...).
# No mutable default literals (= [] or = {}) anywhere in model definitions.

class PipelineState(BaseModel):
    """
    Mutable state object carried through LangGraph.
    frozen=False (Pydantic v2 default) — LangGraph requires direct field assignment.
    validate_assignment=True — every write triggers Pydantic validation.
    """
    model_config = {"validate_assignment": True}

    # ── Identity ──
    project_id: str
    operator_id: str                                         # Telegram user ID
    snapshot_id: Optional[int] = None                        # Time-travel: auto-incremented snapshot number
    program_id: Optional[str] = None                         # Groups related projects (e.g., Unity game + React Native companion)

    # ── Stage Control ──
    current_stage: Stage = Stage.S0_INTAKE
    previous_stage: Optional[Stage] = None
    stage_history: list[dict] = Field(default_factory=list)  # [{stage, entered_at, exited_at}]
    retry_count: int = 0

    # ── Autonomy & Execution ──
    autonomy_mode: AutonomyMode = AutonomyMode.AUTOPILOT
    execution_mode: ExecutionMode = ExecutionMode.CLOUD
    local_heartbeat_alive: bool = False                      # Updated by Heartbeat Monitor

    # ── Stack Selection (set at S2) ──
    selected_stack: Optional[TechStack] = None

    # ── Polymorphic Metadata ──
    # When selected_stack == FLUTTERFLOW:
    #   {"ff_project_id": "...", "ff_api_token": "...", "ff_pages": [...]}
    # When selected_stack == REACT_NATIVE:
    #   {"expo_project_id": "...", "package_json": {...}, "entry_point": "App.tsx"}
    # When selected_stack == SWIFT:
    #   {"xcode_project_path": "...", "bundle_id": "...", "swift_version": "5.10"}
    # ... etc. Schema enforced by StackMetadataValidator at S2.
    project_metadata: dict[str, Any] = Field(default_factory=dict)

    # ── Brand Assets (durable Supabase Storage, not /tmp) ──
    # Each entry: AssetRef dict {asset_type, filename, storage_url, uploaded_at}
    # Populated at S0 Intake: Telegram uploads → Supabase Storage → durable URL stored here.
    # Consumed at S3 (ingest_assets), S6 (icon generation), S7 (verification).
    brand_assets: list[dict] = Field(default_factory=list)

    # ── Continuous Legal Thread ──
    legal_halt: bool = False
    legal_halt_reason: Optional[str] = None
    legal_checks_log: list[dict] = Field(default_factory=list)  # [{stage, check, passed, details, timestamp}]

    # ── Stage Outputs ──
    s0_output: Optional[dict] = None    # Intake requirements
    s1_output: Optional[dict] = None    # Initial legal assessment
    s2_output: Optional[dict] = None    # Blueprint + stack selection + design mocks
    s3_output: Optional[dict] = None    # Generated code/files
    s4_output: Optional[dict] = None    # Build artifacts
    s5_output: Optional[dict] = None    # Test results
    s6_output: Optional[dict] = None    # Deployment URLs
    s7_output: Optional[dict] = None    # Verification results
    s8_output: Optional[dict] = None    # Handoff documentation

    # ── Design Mocks (S2) ──
    design_mocks: list[str] = Field(default_factory=list)     # Paths to 3 PNG mock images

    # ── DocuGen Outputs ──
    legal_documents: dict[str, str] = Field(default_factory=dict)
    # {"privacy_policy": "...", "terms_of_use": "...", "merchant_agreement": "..."}

    # ── War Room State ──
    war_room_active: bool = False
    war_room_history: list[dict] = Field(default_factory=list)  # [{level, error, resolution, cost, timestamp}]

    # ── Budget Tracking ──
    phase_costs: dict[str, float] = Field(default_factory=dict)  # {"S0": 0.45, "S1": 0.80, ...}
    total_cost_usd: float = 0.0
    circuit_breaker_triggered: bool = False

    # ── Warnings & Errors ──
    warnings: list[dict] = Field(default_factory=list)
    errors: list[dict] = Field(default_factory=list)

    # ── Timestamps ──
    created_at: str = ""
    updated_at: str = ""

    def __init__(self, **data):
        super().__init__(**data)
        if not self.created_at:
            self.created_at = datetime.now(timezone.utc).isoformat()
        self.updated_at = datetime.now(timezone.utc).isoformat()
```

#### §2.1.3a AssetRef Model

```python
class AssetRef(BaseModel):
    """Durable reference to a binary asset in Supabase Storage."""
    asset_type: str       # "logo", "screenshot", "voice_memo", "document"
    filename: str         # Original filename from Telegram upload
    storage_url: str      # Supabase Storage URL: project-assets/{project_id}/{filename}
    uploaded_at: datetime  # UTC timestamp of upload

    @validator("asset_type")
    def validate_type(cls, v):
        allowed = {"logo", "screenshot", "voice_memo", "document", "icon", "font", "media"}
        if v not in allowed:
            raise ValueError(f"asset_type must be one of {allowed}")
        return v
```

Binary assets uploaded via Telegram are immediately persisted to Supabase Storage bucket `project-assets/{project_id}/` during S0 intake. The `/tmp` reference is deleted after successful upload. Downstream stages reference `brand_assets[].storage_url` — never local paths.

#### §2.1.3b One-Stack-Per-Project Constraint

Each project selects exactly ONE primary tech stack. The pipeline does not support hybrid builds (e.g., Unity game embedded in React Native wrapper) within a single project.

**Enforcement points:**

1. **S0 Intake:** `validate_single_stack()` rejects any `selected_stack` passed as a list
2. **S1 Legal:** If the brief describes a multi-stack solution, the Strategist splits it into a `program_id` group
3. **S2 Blueprint:** `Blueprint.selected_stack` is a single enum, enforced by Pydantic

```python
@field_validator("selected_stack")
def validate_single_stack(cls, v):
    """Enforce one-stack-per-project constraint."""
    if isinstance(v, list):
        raise ValueError(
            "Exactly one stack per project. For multi-stack apps, "
            "use program_id to group related single-stack projects."
        )
    return v
```

**Multi-stack applications** are split into separate projects linked by `program_id`:

```
Program: "halal-eats" (3 sub-projects)
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Project A: halal-eats-mobile     (REACT_NATIVE)                    │
│   - Consumer app: browse restaurants, order, track delivery         │
│   - Shares: REST API contract with Project C                       │
│                                                                     │
│ Project B: halal-eats-driver     (FLUTTERFLOW)                     │
│   - Driver app: accept orders, navigate, confirm delivery           │
│   - Shares: WebSocket contract with Project C                      │
│                                                                     │
│ Project C: halal-eats-api        (PYTHON_BACKEND)                  │
│   - Backend: order management, restaurant API, payment gateway      │
│   - Shares: REST + WebSocket contracts with Projects A & B          │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

**How it works in practice:**

1. Operator submits brief: "Build a food delivery app like HungerStation"
2. `detect_multi_stack_intent()` triggers at S0 → proposes 3-project split
3. Operator approves → 3 projects created with `program_id="halal-eats"`
4. Each project runs independently through the full S0–S8 pipeline
5. Mother Memory (§6.4) shares API contracts across `program_id` group
6. S8 Handoff delivers 3 separate repos + shared API documentation

**Limitation (deferred):** No automated integration testing between sub-projects. The pipeline generates API contracts but does not verify cross-project compatibility. Operator must validate integration manually or add their own CI/CD integration tests.

```python
async def detect_multi_stack_intent(
    requirements: dict, state: PipelineState
) -> Optional[dict]:
    """At S0/S1: detect if brief describes multi-stack solution.
    If so, propose a program split instead of a single project."""
    indicators = [
        "game" in str(requirements).lower() and "companion" in str(requirements).lower(),
        len(requirements.get("target_platforms", [])) > 2,
        any(w in str(requirements).lower()
            for w in ["backend api + mobile", "web + native", "multiple apps"]),
    ]
    if sum(indicators) >= 2:
        split_proposal = await call_ai(
            role=AIRole.STRATEGIST,
            prompt=(
                f"This project brief describes a multi-stack solution.\n"
                f"Requirements: {json.dumps(requirements, indent=2)}\n\n"
                f"Split into separate single-stack projects. For each sub-project, specify:\n"
                f"- project_suffix (e.g., '-game', '-companion', '-api')\n"
                f"- selected_stack (one TechStack enum)\n"
                f"- shared_interfaces (API contracts between sub-projects)\n"
                f'Return JSON: {{"program_id": "<n>", "sub_projects": [...]}}'
            ),
            state=state,
            action="plan_architecture",
        )
        return json.loads(split_proposal)
    return None
```

#### §2.1.4 Stack Metadata Validators

Each tech stack has a Pydantic model that validates the `project_metadata` dict once the stack is selected at S2:

```python
class FlutterFlowMetadata(BaseModel):
    ff_project_id: str
    ff_pages: list[str]
    ff_collections: list[str]
    ff_api_calls: list[str] = Field(default_factory=list)

class ReactNativeMetadata(BaseModel):
    expo_project_id: Optional[str] = None
    package_json: dict
    entry_point: str = "App.tsx"
    navigation_lib: str = "react-navigation"
    state_management: str = "zustand"

class SwiftMetadata(BaseModel):
    xcode_project_path: str
    bundle_id: str
    swift_version: str = "5.10"
    minimum_ios: str = "16.0"
    uses_swiftui: bool = True

class KotlinMetadata(BaseModel):
    gradle_project_path: str
    package_name: str
    min_sdk: int = 26
    uses_compose: bool = True

class UnityMetadata(BaseModel):
    unity_project_path: str
    unity_version: str
    target_platforms: list[str]   # ["android", "ios", "webgl"]
    render_pipeline: str = "URP"

class PythonBackendMetadata(BaseModel):
    framework: str = "fastapi"
    python_version: str = "3.11"
    database: str = "postgresql"
    deploy_target: str = "cloud_run"

STACK_METADATA_MAP = {
    TechStack.FLUTTERFLOW:    FlutterFlowMetadata,
    TechStack.REACT_NATIVE:   ReactNativeMetadata,
    TechStack.SWIFT:          SwiftMetadata,
    TechStack.KOTLIN:         KotlinMetadata,
    TechStack.UNITY:          UnityMetadata,
    TechStack.PYTHON_BACKEND: PythonBackendMetadata,
}

def validate_stack_metadata(state: PipelineState) -> None:
    """Validate project_metadata matches the selected stack's schema."""
    if state.selected_stack is None:
        raise ValueError("Cannot validate metadata: no stack selected")
    validator_cls = STACK_METADATA_MAP[state.selected_stack]
    validator_cls.model_validate(state.project_metadata)
```

#### §2.1.5 Stage Transition Function

```python
def transition_to(state: PipelineState, target: Stage) -> None:
    """
    The ONLY way to change stages. Enforces the transition map,
    checks for legal halts, records history, resets retry count
    on forward progress.
    """
    # Check continuous legal halt
    if state.legal_halt and target != Stage.HALTED:
        raise IllegalTransition(
            f"Legal halt active: {state.legal_halt_reason}. "
            f"Only transition to HALTED is allowed."
        )

    current = state.current_stage
    allowed = VALID_TRANSITIONS.get(current, [])
    if target not in allowed:
        raise IllegalTransition(
            f"Cannot transition from {current.value} to {target.value}. "
            f"Allowed: {[s.value for s in allowed]}"
        )

    now = datetime.now(timezone.utc).isoformat()

    # Close current stage in history
    if state.stage_history:
        state.stage_history[-1]["exited_at"] = now

    # Open new stage
    state.stage_history.append({
        "stage": target.value,
        "entered_at": now,
        "exited_at": None,
    })

    state.previous_stage = current
    state.current_stage = target
    state.updated_at = now

    # Reset retry count on forward progress (not on loops)
    stage_order = list(Stage)
    if stage_order.index(target) > stage_order.index(current):
        state.retry_count = 0


class IllegalTransition(Exception):
    pass
```

#### §2.1.6 Stage Gate Decorator (with Distributed Locking)

```python
from functools import wraps
from uuid import uuid4
from dataclasses import dataclass, field

# ── Distributed Locking ──
# Prevents duplicate execution when Cloud Run + Cloud Scheduler trigger concurrent workers.
# Uses Postgres advisory locks (existing Supabase — no new dependency).

async def acquire_stage_lock(project_id: str, stage: Stage) -> bool:
    """Acquire advisory lock keyed by (project_id, stage).
    Returns True if lock acquired, False if another worker holds it."""
    lock_key = hash(f"{project_id}:{stage.value}") % (2**31)
    result = await db.execute("SELECT pg_try_advisory_lock($1)", lock_key)
    return result  # True if acquired

async def release_stage_lock(project_id: str, stage: Stage):
    """Release advisory lock. Auto-releases on connection drop (crash safety)."""
    lock_key = hash(f"{project_id}:{stage.value}") % (2**31)
    await db.execute("SELECT pg_advisory_unlock($1)", lock_key)


@dataclass
class StageExecution:
    """Idempotency context for stage execution."""
    stage_run_id: str = field(default_factory=lambda: uuid4().hex)
    project_id: str = ""
    stage: str = ""
    retry_count: int = 0
    dedupe_window_seconds: int = 300  # 5 min — reject duplicate triggers within window


def stage_gate(expected_stage: Stage):
    """
    Decorator that verifies:
    1. Pipeline is in the expected stage
    2. No legal halt is active
    3. No circuit breaker is triggered (without authorization)
    4. Advisory lock acquired (prevents concurrent execution)
    5. Lock released on completion or crash (Postgres auto-releases on disconnect)
    """
    def decorator(fn):
        @wraps(fn)
        async def wrapper(state: PipelineState, *args, **kwargs):
            if state.current_stage != expected_stage:
                raise IllegalTransition(
                    f"Expected stage {expected_stage.value}, "
                    f"got {state.current_stage.value}"
                )
            if state.legal_halt:
                raise IllegalTransition(
                    f"Legal halt active: {state.legal_halt_reason}"
                )
            if state.circuit_breaker_triggered:
                raise BudgetExceeded(
                    f"Circuit breaker triggered. Phase costs: {state.phase_costs}"
                )

            # Acquire distributed lock
            if not await acquire_stage_lock(state.project_id, expected_stage):
                log.warning(
                    f"Stage {expected_stage.value} already running for "
                    f"{state.project_id}, skipping duplicate execution"
                )
                return state  # Another worker has it — safe no-op

            try:
                return await fn(state, *args, **kwargs)
            finally:
                await release_stage_lock(state.project_id, expected_stage)
        return wrapper
    return decorator


class BudgetExceeded(Exception):
    pass
```

**Crash-restart behavior:** If the worker dies mid-stage, the Postgres connection drops, automatically releasing the advisory lock. On restart, `recover_on_startup()` finds the project in a non-terminal stage, acquires the lock, and resumes from the last snapshot. The `dedupe_window_seconds` on `StageExecution` prevents rapid re-triggering. External side effects (AI API calls, store uploads) check for prior completion via idempotency keys before re-executing — no double-billing or double-publishing.

---

### §2.2 AI Role Enforcement (The "Eyes vs. Hands" Doctrine)

#### §2.2.1 Role Contracts

Every AI call goes through a dispatcher that enforces role boundaries:

```python
from dataclasses import dataclass

@dataclass(frozen=True)
class RoleContract:
    """Immutable contract defining what each role can and cannot do."""
    role: AIRole
    model: str
    can_read_web: bool
    can_write_code: bool
    can_write_files: bool
    can_plan_architecture: bool
    can_decide_legal: bool
    can_manage_war_room: bool
    max_output_tokens: int
```

**Model Abstraction Layer:** All model references use `MODEL_CONFIG` lookups. To upgrade models, update env vars without code changes.

```python
import os

MODEL_CONFIG = {
    "strategist":      os.getenv("STRATEGIST_MODEL",       "claude-opus-4-6"),
    "engineer":        os.getenv("ENGINEER_MODEL",          "claude-sonnet-4-5-20250929"),
    "quick_fix":       os.getenv("QUICKFIX_MODEL",          "claude-haiku-4-5-20251001"),
    "gui_supervisor":  os.getenv("GUI_SUPERVISOR_MODEL",    "claude-haiku-4-5-20251001"),
    "scout_search":    os.getenv("SCOUT_MODEL",             "sonar-pro"),
    "scout_reasoning": os.getenv("SCOUT_REASONING_MODEL",   "sonar-reasoning-pro"),
}
```

**Runtime Model Override for Emergency Downgrade (ADR-043):** When set, these override the `MODEL_CONFIG` fallback chain for the corresponding role. Precedence: operator override → Budget Governor degradation → `MODEL_CONFIG` default. Unset = inactive (normal fallback chain). Override validation happens at `call_ai()` dispatch time, not at startup, because the operator may set/unset overrides at any time via env var or Telegram.

```python
MODEL_OVERRIDES = {
    "strategist": os.getenv("STRATEGIST_MODEL_OVERRIDE"),  # e.g., "claude-sonnet-4-5-20250929"
    "engineer":   os.getenv("ENGINEER_MODEL_OVERRIDE"),     # e.g., "claude-haiku-4-5-20251001"
    "quick_fix":  os.getenv("QUICKFIX_MODEL_OVERRIDE"),     # e.g., "claude-haiku-4-5-20251001"
}

VALID_ANTHROPIC_MODELS = {
    "claude-opus-4-6", "claude-opus-4-5-20250929",
    "claude-sonnet-4-5-20250929", "claude-sonnet-4-20250514",
    "claude-haiku-4-5-20251001",
}
```

**Role Contract Definitions:**

```python
ROLE_CONTRACTS = {
    AIRole.SCOUT: RoleContract(
        role=AIRole.SCOUT,
        model=MODEL_CONFIG["scout_search"],
        can_read_web=True,
        can_write_code=False,
        can_write_files=False,
        can_plan_architecture=False,
        can_decide_legal=False,
        can_manage_war_room=False,
        max_output_tokens=4096,
    ),
    AIRole.STRATEGIST: RoleContract(
        role=AIRole.STRATEGIST,
        model=MODEL_CONFIG["strategist"],
        can_read_web=False,      # Strategist uses Scout's intel, not direct search
        can_write_code=False,    # Strategist plans, Engineer executes
        can_write_files=False,
        can_plan_architecture=True,
        can_decide_legal=True,
        can_manage_war_room=True,
        max_output_tokens=8192,
    ),
    AIRole.ENGINEER: RoleContract(
        role=AIRole.ENGINEER,
        model=MODEL_CONFIG["engineer"],
        can_read_web=False,
        can_write_code=True,
        can_write_files=True,
        can_plan_architecture=False,
        can_decide_legal=False,
        can_manage_war_room=False,
        max_output_tokens=16384,
    ),
    AIRole.QUICK_FIX: RoleContract(
        role=AIRole.QUICK_FIX,
        model=MODEL_CONFIG["quick_fix"],
        can_read_web=False,
        can_write_code=True,     # Only syntax-level fixes
        can_write_files=True,    # Only targeted file patches
        can_plan_architecture=False,
        can_decide_legal=False,
        can_manage_war_room=False,
        max_output_tokens=4096,
    ),
}

class RoleViolationError(Exception):
    pass
```

#### §2.2.2 Unified AI Dispatcher

```python
async def call_ai(
    role: AIRole,
    prompt: str,
    state: PipelineState,
    action: str = "general",
) -> str:
    """
    Unified AI dispatcher. Enforces role contracts before any call.
    Tracks costs against the circuit breaker budget (per-role limits).
    Prevents ungrounded research — Scout calls use RESEARCH_DEGRADATION_POLICY.
    External calls check idempotency keys before re-executing after crash recovery.
    """
    contract = ROLE_CONTRACTS[role]

    # ── Check for runtime model override (ADR-043) ──
    override_key = {
        AIRole.STRATEGIST: "strategist",
        AIRole.ENGINEER: "engineer",
        AIRole.QUICK_FIX: "quick_fix",
    }.get(role)

    if override_key:
        override_model = MODEL_OVERRIDES.get(override_key) or os.getenv(
            f"{override_key.upper()}_MODEL_OVERRIDE"
        )
        if override_model:
            if override_model in VALID_ANTHROPIC_MODELS:
                log.warning(
                    f"Model override active: {role.value} → {override_model} "
                    f"(default was {contract.model})"
                )
                # Shallow copy to avoid mutating the shared contract
                contract = RoleContract(**{**contract.__dict__, "model": override_model})
            else:
                log.error(
                    f"Invalid model override '{override_model}' for {role.value}. "
                    f"Valid models: {VALID_ANTHROPIC_MODELS}. Using default: {contract.model}"
                )
                await notify_operator(state, NotificationType.ERROR,
                    f"⚠️ Invalid MODEL_OVERRIDE: '{override_model}' for {role.value}. "
                    f"Using default {contract.model}."
                )

    # ── Budget Governor check (§2.14) ──
    # After MODEL_OVERRIDE, before role enforcement.
    # May degrade contract (AMBER/RED) or raise error (RED intake block, BLACK halt).
    try:
        contract = await budget_governor.check(role, state, contract)
    except BudgetIntakeBlockedError as e:
        log.warning(f"RED tier: intake blocked for {state.project_id}: {e}")
        raise  # Caller handles by queueing the project
    except BudgetExhaustedError as e:
        log.critical(f"BLACK tier: budget exhausted: {e}")
        raise  # Circuit breaker behavior

    # Enforce role boundaries
    if action == "write_code" and not contract.can_write_code:
        raise RoleViolationError(
            f"{role.value} (model={contract.model}) attempted to write code. "
            f"Only ENGINEER and QUICK_FIX roles can write code."
        )
    if action == "plan_architecture" and not contract.can_plan_architecture:
        raise RoleViolationError(
            f"{role.value} attempted to plan architecture. "
            f"Only STRATEGIST can plan architecture."
        )
    if action == "decide_legal" and not contract.can_decide_legal:
        raise RoleViolationError(
            f"{role.value} attempted legal decision. "
            f"Only STRATEGIST can make legal decisions."
        )

    # Route to appropriate provider
    if role == AIRole.SCOUT:
        response, cost = await call_perplexity_safe(prompt, contract, state)
    else:
        response, cost = await call_anthropic(prompt, contract)

    # Track cost against circuit breaker (per-role limits from PHASE_BUDGET_LIMITS)
    phase = state.current_stage.value
    state.phase_costs[phase] = state.phase_costs.get(phase, 0.0) + cost
    state.total_cost_usd += cost

    # Check circuit breaker — per-role limits, not hardcoded $2.00
    role_limit = PHASE_BUDGET_LIMITS.get(role.value, 2.00)
    if state.phase_costs[phase] > role_limit:
        state.circuit_breaker_triggered = True
        await send_telegram_budget_alert(
            state.operator_id,
            phase=phase,
            cost=state.phase_costs[phase],
            limit=role_limit,
        )

    return response
```

#### §2.2.3 Research Degradation Policy ("No Ungrounded Facts")

Any factual claim output by the pipeline must have a `source_id` traceable to a web-grounded search result, a cached verified source in Mother Memory, or an operator-provided document. Claims without sources are tagged `UNVERIFIED` and require operator approval.

```python
RESEARCH_DEGRADATION_POLICY = {
    "primary":    "perplexity_sonar_pro",        # Web-grounded
    "fallback_1": "cached_verified_sources",     # Mother Memory only
    "fallback_2": "operator_provided_sources",   # Manual upload via Telegram
    "fallback_3": "mark_as_UNVERIFIED",          # Requires manual sign-off
    # NEVER: "opus_ungrounded_research"           # Hallucination factory — removed
}
```

**Scout Context-Tier Ceiling (ADR-049):** Prevents accidental large-context queries that inflate costs. Default `"medium"` allows standard search; `"large"` enables deep-research. Controlled by `SCOUT_MAX_CONTEXT_TIER` env var (see §8.9).

```python
SCOUT_MAX_CONTEXT_TIER = os.environ.get("SCOUT_MAX_CONTEXT_TIER", "medium")

CONTEXT_TIER_LIMITS = {
    "small":  {"max_tokens":  4_000, "search_recency": "week",  "max_sources": 3},
    "medium": {"max_tokens": 16_000, "search_recency": "month", "max_sources": 5},
    "large":  {"max_tokens": 64_000, "search_recency": "year",  "max_sources": 10},
}
```

```python
async def call_perplexity_safe(
    prompt: str, contract: RoleContract, state: PipelineState
) -> tuple[str, float]:
    """Safe Perplexity call with degradation policy.
    Never falls back to ungrounded LLM research.
    Enforces SCOUT_MAX_CONTEXT_TIER ceiling before API call."""

    # Enforce context-tier ceiling
    tier = SCOUT_MAX_CONTEXT_TIER
    if tier not in CONTEXT_TIER_LIMITS:
        tier = "medium"  # Safe default
    limits = CONTEXT_TIER_LIMITS[tier]

    if len(prompt) > limits["max_tokens"] * 4:  # Rough char estimate
        prompt = prompt[:limits["max_tokens"] * 4]
        logger.warning(f"Prompt truncated to {tier} tier limit ({limits['max_tokens']} tokens)")

    try:
        return await call_perplexity(prompt, contract, context_tier=tier)
    except PerplexityUnavailableError:
        # Fallback 1: Check Mother Memory for cached verified sources
        cached = await mother_memory.query_verified_sources(prompt, state.project_id)
        if cached:
            return (
                f"[FROM CACHE — source_ids: {[c['source_id'] for c in cached]}] "
                + synthesize_from_cache(cached),
                0.0  # No API cost
            )

        # Fallback 2: Request operator-provided sources
        await notify_operator(state, NotificationType.RESEARCH_NEEDED,
            f"🔍 Research unavailable — Perplexity API is down.\n"
            f"Stage: {state.current_stage.value}\n"
            f"Query: {prompt[:200]}\n\n"
            f"Options:\n"
            f"  /provide_sources — Upload documents for the pipeline to use\n"
            f"  /mark_unverified — Continue with UNVERIFIED status (requires sign-off)\n"
            f"  /wait — Pause and retry Perplexity in 30 minutes"
        )

        # Fallback 3: Mark as UNVERIFIED — pipeline pauses for operator input
        return (
            "[UNVERIFIED — Perplexity unavailable, no cached sources. "
            "Requires operator approval before inclusion in any deliverable.]",
            0.0
        )
```

#### §2.2.4 War Room Escalation Ladder

**Cost Note:** All per-invocation cost estimates in this section (~$0.005 for L1, ~$0.10 for L2, ~$0.50 for L3) are approximate illustrations based on typical token usage. They are not budgetary commitments. Runtime cost enforcement is performed exclusively by the circuit breaker (§3.6) and Budget Governor (§2.14) referencing `BUDGET_CONFIG`.

When the Engineer encounters errors, the War Room protocol escalates through three levels:

```python
class WarRoomLevel(int, Enum):
    L1_QUICK_FIX = 1   # Haiku applies syntax fix
    L2_RESEARCHED = 2  # Scout researches → Sonnet applies fix
    L3_WAR_ROOM = 3    # Opus halts, maps dependencies, supervises rewrite
```

**Level 1 — Quick Fix (Haiku):** Haiku attempts a minimal syntax fix against the error and file content (~$0.005 illustrative). If `apply_and_test_fix()` passes, resolution is logged and execution continues.

**Level 2 — Researched Fix (Scout → Engineer):** Scout researches the error via Perplexity (official docs, known issues, StackOverflow). Sonnet then applies the researched fix (~$0.10 illustrative). If tests pass, resolution is logged.

**Level 3 — War Room (Opus orchestrates):** Opus halts, maps the full dependency tree, identifies the root cause (not the symptom), orders CLI cleanup commands (e.g., `pod deintegrate`, `flutter clean`, `rm -rf node_modules`), and produces a file-by-file rewrite plan. Engineer executes each file rewrite. Cleanup commands pass through `enforce_user_space()` (~$0.50 illustrative).

```python
async def war_room_escalate(
    state: PipelineState,
    error: str,
    error_context: dict,
    current_level: WarRoomLevel = WarRoomLevel.L1_QUICK_FIX,
) -> dict:
    """
    Escalation ladder. Each level is tried in order.
    Returns {"resolved": bool, "level": int, "fix_applied": str, "cost": float}
    """
    total_cost = 0.0

    # ── Level 1: Quick Fix (Haiku) ──
    if current_level <= WarRoomLevel.L1_QUICK_FIX:
        fix = await call_ai(
            role=AIRole.QUICK_FIX,
            prompt=(
                f"Fix this error with minimal changes. "
                f"Error: {error}\n\n"
                f"Context:\n{error_context.get('file_content', '')[:4000]}"
            ),
            state=state, action="write_code",
        )
        success = await apply_and_test_fix(fix, error_context)
        if success:
            state.war_room_history.append({
                "level": 1, "error": error[:300],
                "resolved": True, "timestamp": datetime.now(timezone.utc).isoformat(),
            })
            return {"resolved": True, "level": 1, "fix_applied": fix[:200]}

    # ── Level 2: Researched Fix (Scout → Engineer) ──
    if current_level <= WarRoomLevel.L2_RESEARCHED:
        research = await call_ai(
            role=AIRole.SCOUT,
            prompt=(
                f"Find the solution for this error in official documentation. "
                f"Error: {error}\nStack: {state.selected_stack}\n"
                f"Return: exact fix steps, relevant docs URLs, known issues."
            ),
            state=state, action="general",
        )
        fix = await call_ai(
            role=AIRole.ENGINEER,
            prompt=(
                f"Apply this researched fix.\n\n"
                f"Error: {error}\nResearch findings:\n{research}\n\n"
                f"File content:\n{error_context.get('file_content', '')[:8000]}\n\n"
                f"Return the corrected file content."
            ),
            state=state, action="write_code",
        )
        success = await apply_and_test_fix(fix, error_context)
        if success:
            state.war_room_history.append({
                "level": 2, "error": error[:300], "research": research[:500],
                "resolved": True, "timestamp": datetime.now(timezone.utc).isoformat(),
            })
            return {"resolved": True, "level": 2, "fix_applied": fix[:200]}

    # ── Level 3: War Room (Opus orchestrates) ──
    state.war_room_active = True
    war_room_plan = await call_ai(
        role=AIRole.STRATEGIST,
        prompt=(
            f"WAR ROOM ACTIVATED.\n\n"
            f"Error that survived L1 (quick fix) and L2 (researched fix): {error}\n\n"
            f"Project stack: {state.selected_stack}\n"
            f"Project metadata: {state.project_metadata}\n"
            f"Files involved: {list(error_context.get('files', {}).keys())}\n\n"
            f"Instructions:\n"
            f"1. Map the dependency tree of the failing component.\n"
            f"2. Identify the root cause (not the symptom).\n"
            f"3. Order specific CLI cleanup commands if needed "
            f"   (e.g., pod deintegrate, flutter clean, rm -rf node_modules).\n"
            f"4. Produce a file-by-file rewrite plan listing each file, "
            f"   what's wrong, and the exact fix.\n\n"
            f"Return JSON:\n"
            f'{{"root_cause": "...", "cleanup_commands": [...], '
            f'"rewrite_plan": [{{"file": "...", "issue": "...", "fix": "..."}}]}}'
        ),
        state=state, action="plan_architecture",
    )

    plan = json.loads(war_room_plan)

    # Execute cleanup commands (user-space enforced)
    for cmd in plan.get("cleanup_commands", []):
        validated_cmd = enforce_user_space(cmd)
        await execute_command(validated_cmd)

    # Execute file-by-file rewrites via Engineer
    for rewrite in plan.get("rewrite_plan", []):
        fix = await call_ai(
            role=AIRole.ENGINEER,
            prompt=(
                f"Rewrite this file per the War Room plan.\n\n"
                f"File: {rewrite['file']}\n"
                f"Issue: {rewrite['issue']}\n"
                f"Required fix: {rewrite['fix']}\n\n"
                f"Current content:\n"
                f"{error_context.get('files', {}).get(rewrite['file'], 'N/A')[:8000]}"
            ),
            state=state, action="write_code",
        )
        await write_file(rewrite["file"], fix)

    success = await run_tests(error_context)
    state.war_room_active = False
    state.war_room_history.append({
        "level": 3, "error": error[:300], "plan": plan,
        "resolved": success, "timestamp": datetime.now(timezone.utc).isoformat(),
    })
    return {"resolved": success, "level": 3, "plan": plan}
```

**If L3 fails:** The pipeline pauses and alerts the operator. If a GUI-dependent stack hits L3 three times, the Stack Pivot Protocol (§2.3.2) proposes switching to a CLI-native stack. All War Room sessions are logged as `WarRoomEvent` nodes in Neo4j for cross-project learning.

---

### §2.3 Stack Selector Brain

The Stack Selector runs at S2. It is the Strategist's (Opus 4.6) first major decision.

#### §2.3.1 Selection Criteria

```python
STACK_SELECTION_CRITERIA = {
    TechStack.FLUTTERFLOW: {
        "best_for": [
            "Standard CRUD apps (todo, booking, inventory)",
            "Rapid MVP (need result in <1 hour)",
            "Non-technical operator wants visual control post-delivery",
            "Simple e-commerce or catalog apps",
        ],
        "avoid_when": [
            "Custom native APIs (ARKit, HealthKit, CameraX)",
            "Complex animations or custom rendering",
            "Existing codebase to integrate with",
            "Game or 3D application",
        ],
        "build_toolchain": "FlutterFlow API + GUI Agent + Flutter CLI",
        "requires_gui_automation": True,
        "requires_macincloud": True,
    },
    TechStack.REACT_NATIVE: {
        "best_for": [
            "Complex custom UI with JS ecosystem",
            "Apps needing web + mobile parity",
            "Projects requiring many npm packages",
            "Social media / content-heavy apps",
        ],
        "avoid_when": [
            "Heavy native performance (games, video editing)",
            "Operator needs visual IDE control",
        ],
        "build_toolchain": "Expo CLI + Metro + EAS Build",
        "requires_gui_automation": False,
        "requires_macincloud": True,
    },
    TechStack.SWIFT: {
        "best_for": [
            "iOS-only premium experiences",
            "ARKit, HealthKit, Core ML, widgets",
            "App Store feature requirements",
        ],
        "avoid_when": [
            "Need Android or Web simultaneously",
            "Rapid MVP (longer build cycle)",
        ],
        "build_toolchain": "Xcode + SwiftPM + xcodebuild",
        "requires_gui_automation": False,
        "requires_macincloud": True,
    },
    TechStack.KOTLIN: {
        "best_for": [
            "Android-only with Jetpack Compose",
            "Google Play-specific features",
            "Android Automotive, Wear OS",
        ],
        "avoid_when": ["Need iOS simultaneously"],
        "build_toolchain": "Gradle + Android SDK + Kotlin DSL",
        "requires_gui_automation": False,
        "requires_macincloud": False,
    },
    TechStack.UNITY: {
        "best_for": [
            "Games (2D or 3D)", "AR/VR applications",
            "Interactive simulations",
        ],
        "avoid_when": [
            "Standard business apps (overkill)",
            "Budget-constrained (Unity builds are heavy)",
        ],
        "build_toolchain": "Unity Editor CLI + IL2CPP",
        "requires_gui_automation": True,
        "requires_macincloud": True,
    },
    TechStack.PYTHON_BACKEND: {
        "best_for": [
            "API-only services", "Data pipelines, ML inference",
            "Backend for existing frontend",
        ],
        "avoid_when": ["Need mobile app UI", "Need client-side functionality"],
        "build_toolchain": "FastAPI + Docker + Cloud Run",
        "requires_gui_automation": False,
        "requires_macincloud": False,
    },
}
```

```python
async def select_stack(
    state: PipelineState,
    requirements: dict,
    legal_output: dict,
) -> TechStack:
    """Strategist (Opus 4.6) selects the optimal stack. Uses Scout intel for framework research."""

    scout_intel = await call_ai(
        role=AIRole.SCOUT,
        prompt=(
            f"Best mobile/web framework for: {requirements.get('app_description', '')}?\n"
            f"Features: {requirements.get('features_must', [])}\n"
            f"Platforms: {requirements.get('target_platforms', [])}\n"
            f"Compare: FlutterFlow, React Native, native Swift/Kotlin, Unity, Python backend.\n"
            f"Return pros/cons for each relevant option."
        ),
        state=state, action="general",
    )

    decision = await call_ai(
        role=AIRole.STRATEGIST,
        prompt=(
            f"SELECT THE OPTIMAL TECH STACK.\n\n"
            f"App requirements:\n{json.dumps(requirements, indent=2)}\n\n"
            f"Legal constraints:\n{json.dumps(legal_output, indent=2)}\n\n"
            f"Framework research:\n{scout_intel}\n\n"
            f"Available stacks:\n"
            f"{json.dumps({k.value: v for k, v in STACK_SELECTION_CRITERIA.items()}, indent=2)}\n\n"
            f"Execution mode: {state.execution_mode.value}\n"
            f"(If LOCAL mode, prefer stacks that can build locally.)\n\n"
            f'Return JSON: {{"selected_stack": "<enum>", "reasoning": "...", '
            f'"alternatives_considered": ["<stack>: <why rejected>"]}}'
        ),
        state=state, action="plan_architecture",
    )

    result = json.loads(decision)
    selected = TechStack(result["selected_stack"])
    state.selected_stack = selected
    return selected
```

#### §2.3.2 GUI Stack Pivot Protocol

If GUI automation fails 3 consecutive times for a GUI-dependent stack (FlutterFlow, Unity), the War Room escalates to L3 and proposes a CLI-native pivot.

```python
GUI_FAILURE_THRESHOLD = 3  # Consecutive failures before pivot proposal

# Modifiers applied to the Strategist's stack scoring when the pipeline
# has historical GUI failure data for this operator.
STACK_SCORE_MODIFIERS = {
    "cli_native_bonus":       +15,  # Bonus for stacks that don't need GUI automation
    "gui_automation_penalty": -10,  # Penalty for stacks requiring GUI when history shows failures
}


async def check_gui_pivot(
    state: PipelineState, gui_error: str
) -> Optional[str]:
    """Check if GUI failures have hit threshold. If so, propose CLI-native pivot.
    Returns pivot proposal string, or None if under threshold."""

    failures = await supabase_client.table("gui_failure_log") \
        .select("count") \
        .eq("project_id", state.project_id) \
        .eq("resolved", False) \
        .execute()

    failure_count = failures.data[0]["count"] if failures.data else 0

    if failure_count >= GUI_FAILURE_THRESHOLD:
        # Escalate to War Room L3
        await war_room_escalate(
            state=state,
            error=f"GUI automation failed {failure_count} times: {gui_error}",
            error_context={"type": "gui_pivot", "failure_count": failure_count},
            current_level=WarRoomLevel.L3_WAR_ROOM,
        )

        cli_alternatives = [
            stack.value for stack, config in STACK_SELECTION_CRITERIA.items()
            if not config.get("requires_gui_automation", False)
            and stack != state.selected_stack
        ]

        pivot_msg = (
            f"🔧 **Stack Pivot Proposal**\n\n"
            f"GUI automation failed {failure_count} times for {state.selected_stack.value}.\n"
            f"CLI-native alternatives: {', '.join(cli_alternatives)}\n\n"
            f"Options:\n"
            f"  /pivot <stack> — Switch to CLI-native stack\n"
            f"  /override — Continue with {state.selected_stack.value} (operator fixes GUI manually)\n"
            f"  /cancel — Stop project"
        )
        await notify_operator(state, NotificationType.WAR_ROOM, pivot_msg)
        return pivot_msg

    return None
```

**Scoring impact:** When `select_stack()` runs for a new project and the operator has a history of GUI failures (>2 in last 30 days), the Strategist receives `STACK_SCORE_MODIFIERS` as additional context: CLI-native stacks get a +15 bonus, GUI-dependent stacks get a −10 penalty. The operator can override with `/force_stack <name>`.

## Part 4: Three-Mode Execution, User-Space Enforcer, Blueprint & LangGraph DAG

---

### §2.4 Three-Mode Execution Layer

Every command the pipeline executes — builds, deploys, file writes, CLI invocations — is routed through the Execution Mode Manager. The operator selects their mode via Telegram toggle. Default: Cloud Mode.

#### §2.4.1 Execution Mode Manager

```python
class ExecutionModeManager:
    """
    Manages Cloud / Local / Hybrid execution.
    Operator selects mode via Telegram toggle.
    Default: Cloud Mode.
    """
    def __init__(self, state: PipelineState):
        self.state = state

    async def execute_task(
        self, task: dict, requires_macincloud: bool, requires_gpu: bool = False,
    ) -> dict:
        """Route task execution based on current mode."""
        mode = self.state.execution_mode

        if mode == ExecutionMode.CLOUD:
            return await self._execute_cloud(task, requires_macincloud)

        elif mode == ExecutionMode.LOCAL:
            if not self.state.local_heartbeat_alive:
                await self._notify_failover("Local machine unreachable")
                return await self._execute_cloud(task, requires_macincloud)
            return await self._execute_local(task)

        elif mode == ExecutionMode.HYBRID:
            return await self._execute_hybrid(task, requires_macincloud, requires_gpu)

    async def _execute_cloud(self, task: dict, requires_mac: bool) -> dict:
        """GitHub Actions (Linux) for Web/Android, MacinCloud PAYG for iOS + GUI."""
        if requires_mac:
            session = await acquire_macincloud_session(purpose=task["name"])
            try:
                result = await run_on_macincloud(session, task)
            finally:
                await release_macincloud_session(session["id"])
            return result
        else:
            return await trigger_github_action(task)

    async def _execute_local(self, task: dict) -> dict:
        """Send commands to operator's machine via Cloudflare Tunnel. Cost: $0."""
        tunnel_url = await get_tunnel_url(self.state.operator_id)
        return await send_command_via_tunnel(
            tunnel_url=tunnel_url,
            command=task["command"],
            working_dir=task.get("working_dir", "~/factory-workspace"),
            timeout=task.get("timeout", 600),
        )

    async def _execute_hybrid(
        self, task: dict, requires_mac: bool, requires_gpu: bool,
    ) -> dict:
        """Cloud does backend/infra, local does heavy rendering/compilation."""
        if task.get("type") == "backend_deploy":
            return await self._execute_cloud(task, requires_mac=False)
        elif task.get("type") in ("ios_build", "gui_automation", "heavy_render"):
            if self.state.local_heartbeat_alive:
                return await self._execute_local(task)
            else:
                return await self._execute_cloud(task, requires_mac=True)
        else:
            return await self._execute_cloud(task, requires_mac)

    async def _notify_failover(self, reason: str) -> None:
        original = self.state.execution_mode.value
        self.state.execution_mode = ExecutionMode.CLOUD
        await send_telegram_message(
            self.state.operator_id,
            f"⚠️ {reason}. Switched {original} → Cloud Mode.\n"
            f"Pipeline continues uninterrupted.",
        )
```

**Mode routing summary:**

| Mode | Linux tasks | macOS tasks (iOS/GUI) | Heavy render/GPU |
|------|------------|----------------------|------------------|
| Cloud | GitHub Actions | MacinCloud PAYG | MacinCloud PAYG |
| Local | Cloudflare Tunnel → operator machine | Cloudflare Tunnel → operator Mac | Cloudflare Tunnel |
| Hybrid | GitHub Actions (cloud) | Operator Mac if alive, else MacinCloud | Operator machine if alive, else cloud |

**Failover:** In Local and Hybrid modes, if the heartbeat monitor detects the operator's machine is unreachable (3 consecutive failures = 90 seconds), the pipeline automatically switches to Cloud Mode and notifies the operator via Telegram. The pipeline never blocks waiting for local connectivity.

#### §2.4.2 Heartbeat Monitor

```python
class HeartbeatMonitor:
    """
    Pings local agent every 30 seconds.
    3 consecutive failures (90s) → auto-switch to Cloud Mode.
    """
    def __init__(self, state: PipelineState):
        self.state = state
        self.consecutive_failures = 0
        self.max_failures = 3

    async def ping(self) -> bool:
        try:
            tunnel_url = await get_tunnel_url(self.state.operator_id)
            async with httpx.AsyncClient(timeout=10) as client:
                resp = await client.get(f"{tunnel_url}/heartbeat")
                if resp.status_code == 200:
                    self.consecutive_failures = 0
                    self.state.local_heartbeat_alive = True
                    return True
        except Exception:
            pass

        self.consecutive_failures += 1
        if self.consecutive_failures >= self.max_failures:
            self.state.local_heartbeat_alive = False
            if self.state.execution_mode != ExecutionMode.CLOUD:
                self.state.execution_mode = ExecutionMode.CLOUD
                await send_telegram_message(
                    self.state.operator_id,
                    f"🔴 Local machine unreachable (3 missed heartbeats).\n"
                    f"Auto-switched to Cloud Mode.",
                )
        return False

async def heartbeat_loop(state: PipelineState) -> None:
    """Background task running during pipeline execution."""
    monitor = HeartbeatMonitor(state)
    while state.current_stage not in (Stage.S8_HANDOFF, Stage.HALTED):
        await monitor.ping()
        await asyncio.sleep(30)
```

#### §2.4.3 Local Agent

A minimal HTTP server that runs on the operator's machine. Exposed via Cloudflare Tunnel. All commands execute in user space — `sudo` is prohibited.

```python
# factory_agent.py — Minimal HTTP server on operator's machine
# Install: pip install fastapi uvicorn --user
# Expose: cloudflared tunnel run factory-agent (localhost:8765)
from fastapi import FastAPI
import subprocess, os

app = FastAPI()
WORKSPACE = os.path.expanduser("~/factory-workspace")
os.makedirs(WORKSPACE, exist_ok=True)

@app.get("/heartbeat")
async def heartbeat():
    return {"status": "alive", "workspace": WORKSPACE}

@app.post("/execute")
async def execute(command: str, working_dir: str = WORKSPACE):
    """Execute in user space. NEVER runs sudo."""
    if "sudo" in command or "su " in command:
        return {"error": "sudo is prohibited", "exit_code": -1}
    result = subprocess.run(
        command, shell=True, cwd=working_dir,
        capture_output=True, text=True, timeout=600,
        env={**os.environ, "PATH": f"{WORKSPACE}/.local/bin:{os.environ['PATH']}"},
    )
    return {
        "stdout": result.stdout[-5000:],
        "stderr": result.stderr[-2000:],
        "exit_code": result.returncode,
    }

@app.post("/upload")
async def upload_file(path: str, content: str):
    full_path = os.path.join(WORKSPACE, path)
    os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(full_path), exist_ok=True)
    with open(full_path, "w") as f:
        f.write(content)
    return {"written": full_path}
```

---

### §2.5 User-Space Enforcer (Zero Sudo)

Every command the pipeline generates — whether for cloud, local, or hybrid execution — passes through the User-Space Enforcer before execution. This is a hard security boundary.

```python
PROHIBITED_PATTERNS = [
    "sudo ", "sudo\t", "su -", "su root", "pkexec", "doas ",
    "chmod 777", "chmod +s", "chown root", "/usr/sbin/",
    "rm -rf /", "dd if=",
]

SAFE_INSTALL_REWRITES = {
    "pip install": "pip install --user",
    "npm install -g": "npx",
}

def enforce_user_space(command: str) -> str:
    """
    Validate and sanitize a command for user-space execution.
    Raises UserSpaceViolation if prohibited pattern detected.
    """
    command_lower = command.lower().strip()

    for pattern in PROHIBITED_PATTERNS:
        if pattern in command_lower:
            raise UserSpaceViolation(
                f"Prohibited pattern '{pattern}' in command: {command[:100]}"
            )

    # Rewrite global installs to user-space equivalents
    for old, new in SAFE_INSTALL_REWRITES.items():
        if old in command and new not in command:
            command = command.replace(old, new)

    return command

class UserSpaceViolation(Exception):
    pass
```

**Prohibited patterns** block: `sudo`, `su`, `pkexec`, `doas`, `chmod 777`, `chmod +s`, `chown root`, `/usr/sbin/` paths, destructive `rm -rf /`, and raw `dd` writes. **Rewrite rules** transparently convert `pip install` to `pip install --user` and `npm install -g` to `npx` — no global installs.

---

### §2.6 Blueprint Schema (Polyglot)

The Blueprint is the master specification generated at S2. It is consumed by every downstream stage (S3–S8). It is stack-agnostic in structure, with stack-specific configuration stored in `stack_config`.

```python
class Blueprint(BaseModel):
    """Master specification generated at S2. Consumed by S3–S8."""
    model_config = {"validate_assignment": True}

    project_id: str
    app_name: str
    app_description: str
    target_platforms: list[str]
    selected_stack: TechStack

    # Universal fields (all stacks)
    screens: list[dict]
    data_model: list[dict]
    api_endpoints: list[dict]
    auth_method: str
    payment_mode: str = "SANDBOX"
    legal_classification: str
    data_residency: str = "KSA"

    # Stack-specific config
    stack_config: dict = Field(default_factory=dict)

    # Design
    color_palette: dict = Field(default_factory=dict)
    typography: dict = Field(default_factory=dict)
    design_system: str = "material3"

    # Legal
    business_model: Optional[str] = None
    required_legal_docs: list[str] = Field(default_factory=list)
    generated_by: list[str] = Field(default_factory=list)

    @model_validator(mode="after")
    def enforce_sandbox_default(self):
        if self.payment_mode == "PRODUCTION":
            pass  # Checked at runtime via Mother Memory approval
        return self

    @model_validator(mode="after")
    def validate_screen_data_bindings(self):
        collection_names = {c["collection"] for c in self.data_model}
        for screen in self.screens:
            for binding in screen.get("data_bindings", []):
                if binding.get("collection") and binding["collection"] not in collection_names:
                    raise ValueError(
                        f"Screen '{screen['name']}' binds to '{binding['collection']}' "
                        f"which doesn't exist in data_model."
                    )
        return self
```

**Blueprint validators:**

1. **`enforce_sandbox_default`** — `payment_mode` defaults to `"SANDBOX"`. Production mode requires explicit Mother Memory approval (see §6.5).
2. **`validate_screen_data_bindings`** — Every screen `data_bindings[].collection` must reference a valid collection name from `data_model`. Catches orphaned screen bindings at blueprint validation time, not at build time.

---

### §2.7 LangGraph DAG

#### §2.7.1 DAG Topology

The pipeline is implemented as a LangGraph `StateGraph` carrying `PipelineState`. The graph is linear S0→S8 with two conditional back-edges for error recovery.

```python
from langgraph.graph import StateGraph, END

def build_pipeline_graph() -> StateGraph:
    graph = StateGraph(PipelineState)

    graph.add_node("s0_intake",    s0_intake_node)
    graph.add_node("s1_legal",     s1_legal_node)
    graph.add_node("s2_blueprint", s2_blueprint_node)
    graph.add_node("s3_codegen",   s3_codegen_node)
    graph.add_node("s4_build",     s4_build_node)
    graph.add_node("s5_test",      s5_test_node)
    graph.add_node("s6_deploy",    s6_deploy_node)
    graph.add_node("s7_verify",    s7_verify_node)
    graph.add_node("s8_handoff",   s8_handoff_node)
    graph.add_node("halt_handler", halt_handler_node)

    graph.set_entry_point("s0_intake")
    graph.add_edge("s0_intake",    "s1_legal")
    graph.add_edge("s1_legal",     "s2_blueprint")
    graph.add_edge("s2_blueprint", "s3_codegen")
    graph.add_edge("s3_codegen",   "s4_build")
    graph.add_edge("s4_build",     "s5_test")

    # After S5 Test: pass → S6 Deploy (via pre-deploy gate), fail → S3 retry, fatal → halt
    graph.add_conditional_edges("s5_test", route_after_test, {
        "s6_deploy":  "s6_deploy",   # pre_deploy_gate() checked inside router (ADR-046)
        "s3_codegen": "s3_codegen",  # Fix loop: War Room → regen → rebuild → retest
        "halt":       "halt_handler",
    })

    graph.add_edge("s6_deploy", "s7_verify")

    # After S7 Verify: pass → S8 Handoff, fail → S6 redeploy, fatal → halt
    graph.add_conditional_edges("s7_verify", route_after_verify, {
        "s8_handoff": "s8_handoff",
        "s6_deploy":  "s6_deploy",   # Redeploy with fixes
        "halt":       "halt_handler",
    })

    graph.add_edge("s8_handoff",   END)
    graph.add_edge("halt_handler", END)

    return graph.compile()
```

**Back-edge semantics:**

- **S5→S3 loop (fix cycle):** When tests fail, the War Room attempts fixes at escalating levels (§2.2.8). If a fix is found, the pipeline loops back to S3 (codegen) to regenerate, then S4 (build), then S5 (retest). The `retry_count` on `PipelineState` tracks loop iterations; after the configured maximum (default 3), the pipeline halts.
- **S7→S6 loop (redeploy):** When post-deploy verification fails (e.g., health check fails, deployment URL unreachable), the pipeline re-deploys. After the configured maximum retries, the pipeline halts.

#### §2.7.2 Node Wrapper (Legal Hook + Snapshot)

Every DAG node is wrapped with the continuous legal thread and snapshot persistence:

```python
def pipeline_node(stage: Stage):
    """Decorator that wraps every DAG node with legal checks,
    snapshots, and budget tracking."""
    def decorator(fn):
        @wraps(fn)
        async def wrapper(state: PipelineState) -> PipelineState:
            # Pre-stage legal check
            await legal_check_hook(state, stage, "pre")
            if state.legal_halt:
                transition_to(state, Stage.HALTED)
                return state

            # Execute the actual stage logic
            transition_to(state, stage)
            state = await fn(state)

            # Post-stage legal check
            await legal_check_hook(state, stage, "post")
            if state.legal_halt:
                transition_to(state, Stage.HALTED)
                return state

            # Persist snapshot (time-travel)
            await persist_state(state)

            return state
        return wrapper
    return decorator
```

#### §2.7.3 Continuous Legal Thread

Legal compliance checks run at specific stages, both before and after execution. They do not appear as pipeline stages — they are injected by the `pipeline_node` wrapper.

```python
LEGAL_CHECKS_BY_STAGE = {
    Stage.S2_BLUEPRINT: {
        "pre":  ["ministry_of_commerce_licensing"],
        "post": ["blueprint_legal_compliance"],
    },
    Stage.S3_CODEGEN: {
        "post": ["pdpl_consent_checkboxes", "data_residency_compliance"],
    },
    Stage.S4_BUILD: {
        "post": ["no_prohibited_sdks"],
    },
    Stage.S6_DEPLOY: {
        "pre":  ["cst_time_of_day_restrictions"],
        "post": ["deployment_region_compliance"],
    },
    Stage.S8_HANDOFF: {
        "post": ["all_legal_docs_generated", "final_compliance_sign_off"],
    },
}

async def legal_check_hook(state: PipelineState, stage: Stage, phase: str) -> None:
    """Run legal checks for a given stage/phase. Uses Scout + Strategist."""
    checks = LEGAL_CHECKS_BY_STAGE.get(stage, {}).get(phase, [])
    for check_name in checks:
        result = await run_legal_check(state, check_name)
        state.legal_checks_log.append({
            "stage": stage.value, "phase": phase,
            "check": check_name, "passed": result["passed"],
            "details": result.get("details"),
            "timestamp": datetime.now(timezone.utc).isoformat(),
        })
        if not result["passed"] and result.get("blocking", True):
            state.legal_halt = True
            state.legal_halt_reason = (
                f"'{check_name}' failed at {stage.value}/{phase}: "
                f"{result.get('details', 'No details')}"
            )
            await send_telegram_message(
                state.operator_id,
                f"🚨 Legal compliance issue:\n\n"
                f"Check: {check_name}\nStage: {stage.value}\n"
                f"Details: {result.get('details', 'N/A')}\n\n"
                f"Pipeline paused. Reply /continue after resolving.",
            )
            return
```

**Legal check semantics:**

| Stage | Phase | Check | What it does |
|-------|-------|-------|-------------|
| S2 | pre | `ministry_of_commerce_licensing` | Verifies business license requirements for the app category |
| S2 | post | `blueprint_legal_compliance` | Validates blueprint against KSA legal requirements |
| S3 | post | `pdpl_consent_checkboxes` | Ensures PDPL consent UI is present in generated code |
| S3 | post | `data_residency_compliance` | Validates data storage is KSA-resident |
| S4 | post | `no_prohibited_sdks` | Scans build dependencies for sanctioned/prohibited SDKs |
| S6 | pre | `cst_time_of_day_restrictions` | Prevents deployment outside allowed hours (configurable) |
| S6 | post | `deployment_region_compliance` | Validates deployment target is in allowed regions |
| S8 | post | `all_legal_docs_generated` | Confirms all required legal documents were produced |
| S8 | post | `final_compliance_sign_off` | Final compliance sweep before handoff |

---

### §2.8 Regulatory Body Resolution

Saudi regulatory body names have multiple aliases. The pipeline normalizes all references to canonical identifiers:

```python
REGULATORY_BODY_MAPPING: dict[str, str] = {
    "CITC": "CST",
    "COMMUNICATIONS AND INFORMATION TECHNOLOGY COMMISSION": "CST",
    "COMMUNICATIONS, SPACE & TECHNOLOGY COMMISSION": "CST",
    "SAMA": "SAMA",
    "SAUDI ARABIAN MONETARY AUTHORITY": "SAMA",
    "SAUDI CENTRAL BANK": "SAMA",
    "NDMO": "NDMO",
    "NATIONAL DATA MANAGEMENT OFFICE": "NDMO",
    "NCA": "NCA",
    "NATIONAL CYBERSECURITY AUTHORITY": "NCA",
    "SDAIA": "SDAIA",
    "SAUDI DATA AND AI AUTHORITY": "SDAIA",
    "SAUDI DATA & AI AUTHORITY": "SDAIA",
    "MINISTRY OF COMMERCE": "MINISTRY_OF_COMMERCE",
    "MOC": "MINISTRY_OF_COMMERCE",
}

def resolve_regulatory_body(name: str) -> str:
    normalized = name.strip().upper()
    return REGULATORY_BODY_MAPPING.get(normalized, normalized)
```
