### §6.7 State Consistency

**Write order:** Stage logic → Post-legal → Supabase current → Supabase snapshot → GitHub → Backfill hash. If steps 4–6 fail, current state is safe; next `persist` creates a new snapshot.

```python
async def repair_missing_snapshots(project_id: str) -> int:
    snaps = (
        await supabase_client.table("state_snapshots")
        .select("snapshot_id")
        .eq("project_id", project_id)
        .order("snapshot_id").execute()
    )
    if not snaps.data:
        return 0

    ids = [s["snapshot_id"] for s in snaps.data]
    missing = set(range(ids[0], ids[-1] + 1)) - set(ids)

    for mid in sorted(missing):
        nearest = (
            await supabase_client.table("state_snapshots")
            .select("*")
            .eq("project_id", project_id)
            .lt("snapshot_id", mid)
            .order("snapshot_id", desc=True)
            .limit(1).execute()
        )
        if nearest.data:
            await supabase_client.table("state_snapshots").insert({
                "project_id": project_id,
                "snapshot_id": mid,
                "stage": nearest.data[0]["stage"],
                "state_json": nearest.data[0]["state_json"],
                "created_at": nearest.data[0]["created_at"],
            }).execute()

    return len(missing)
```

#### §6.7.1 Vector Search Backend (v5.5 — C8 + FIX-13)

**[C8] Default:** `VECTOR_BACKEND=pgvector` — Supabase pgvector (GA, production-stable, existing dependency, no new cost).

**Opt-in:** `VECTOR_BACKEND=neo4j_vector` — Neo4j AuraDB vector indexes (Public Preview as of Feb 2026 [V15] — not recommended for production). Neo4j remains the default for graph queries (relationship traversal, pattern detection) which are GA.

**[FIX-13] Public Preview Caveat:** "Public Preview" means Neo4j has released vector index functionality for evaluation but has not committed to GA stability guarantees. Specific risks:

1. API breaking changes — vector index syntax (`db.index.vector.queryNodes`) may change without deprecation notice between Neo4j minor versions
2. Performance characteristics unguaranteed — query latency, memory usage, and index build times may vary significantly between Preview releases
3. Data migration risk — vector indexes may require recreation (not in-place migration) on version upgrades
4. No SLA coverage — Neo4j AuraDB SLA covers GA features only; vector index outages may not be covered
5. Timeline unknown — GA date is unconfirmed as of Feb 2026 [V15]; Preview status could persist for months

**Recommendation:** Use pgvector (default) for production. Use `neo4j_vector` only in development/staging environments for evaluation purposes. If you opt in to `neo4j_vector` in production, monitor the Neo4j changelog before every AuraDB version upgrade.

**Rationale (ADR-041 updated):** Neo4j vector search is Public Preview. Using GA technology as default is the safest approach. When Neo4j vector search reaches GA status, re-evaluate defaulting to it for unified graph+vector queries.

```python
# [C8] Default flipped from "neo4j" to "pgvector"
#      — Public Preview → GA default
VECTOR_BACKEND = os.getenv("VECTOR_BACKEND", "pgvector")
# Options:
#   "pgvector"      (default, GA, production-stable)
#   "neo4j_vector"  (opt-in, Public Preview, use at own risk)


async def vector_search(
    query_embedding: list[float], top_k: int = 5,
) -> list[dict]:
    if VECTOR_BACKEND == "pgvector":
        # [C8] Default: Supabase pgvector (GA)
        result = await supabase_client.rpc(
            "match_components",
            {
                "query_embedding": query_embedding,
                "match_threshold": 0.7,
                "match_count": top_k,
            },
        ).execute()
        return result.data
    else:
        # Opt-in: Neo4j vector (Public Preview)
        return await neo4j_run("""
            CALL db.index.vector.queryNodes(
                'component_embeddings', $top_k, $embedding
            ) YIELD node, score
            RETURN node, score ORDER BY score DESC
        """, {"top_k": top_k, "embedding": query_embedding})

# Rollback: Set VECTOR_BACKEND=neo4j_vector via env var.
# Instant revert, no code change needed.
#
# Monitoring: The Janitor Agent's collect_memory_stats()
# tracks vector query latency. Alert if p95 > 500ms.
# Monitor via memory_stats table.
```

---

*End of Part 10 — PART 6 (Memory & State) complete. Reply "Cont" for Part 11 (PART 7: Operations & Safety — Setup Protocol, Local Mode, Disaster Recovery, Monitoring, App Store Airlock, Security, Final Assembly).*

## §7.1.2 Automated Setup Script

The setup wizard is an interactive Telegram-based process. It collects API keys, verifies each service connection, initializes databases, and registers the operator. The entire flow happens via Telegram messages — no terminal required.

```python
async def run_setup_wizard(operator_id: str) -> dict:
    """
    Interactive Telegram-based setup wizard.
    Verifies each service, stores secrets, initializes databases.
    """
    results = {"passed": [], "failed": [], "skipped": []}

    await send_telegram_message(operator_id,
        "🏭 AI Factory v5.6 Setup Wizard\n\n"
        "I'll verify each service connection.\n"
        "Have your API keys ready."
    )

    # ── Step 1: Collect API keys ──
    secrets_needed = [
        ("ANTHROPIC_API_KEY", "Anthropic API key (from console.anthropic.com/settings/keys)"),
        ("PERPLEXITY_API_KEY", "Perplexity API key (from perplexity.ai/settings/api)"),
        ("SUPABASE_URL", "Supabase project URL (from Settings > API)"),
        ("SUPABASE_SERVICE_KEY", "Supabase service role key"),
        ("NEO4J_URI", "Neo4j Aura connection URI (neo4j+s://xxx.databases.neo4j.io)"),
        ("NEO4J_PASSWORD", "Neo4j password"),
        ("GITHUB_TOKEN", "GitHub personal access token (repo + workflow scopes)"),
        ("TELEGRAM_BOT_TOKEN", "Telegram bot token (from @BotFather)"),
    ]

    for key_name, description in secrets_needed:
        await send_telegram_message(operator_id, f"🔑 Send me your {description}:")
        value = await wait_for_operator_reply(operator_id, timeout=300, default="SKIP")
        if value == "SKIP":
            results["skipped"].append(key_name)
            continue
        # Store in GCP Secret Manager
        await store_secret(key_name, value)
        results["passed"].append(key_name)

    # ── Step 2: Verify connections ──
    verifications = [
        ("Anthropic", verify_anthropic),
        ("Perplexity", verify_perplexity),
        ("Supabase", verify_supabase),
        ("Neo4j", verify_neo4j),
        ("GitHub", verify_github),
    ]

    for name, verify_fn in verifications:
        try:
            await verify_fn()
            results["passed"].append(f"{name}_connection")
            await send_telegram_message(operator_id, f"✅ {name} connected")
        except Exception as e:
            results["failed"].append(f"{name}_connection: {str(e)[:100]}")
            await send_telegram_message(operator_id, f"❌ {name} failed: {str(e)[:100]}")

    # ── Step 3: Initialize databases ──
    if "Supabase_connection" not in [r for r in results["failed"]]:
        await initialize_supabase_schema()
        await send_telegram_message(operator_id, "🗄️ Supabase tables created")

    if "Neo4j_connection" not in [r for r in results["failed"]]:
        await initialize_neo4j_schema()
        await send_telegram_message(operator_id, "🕸️ Neo4j indexes created")

    # ── Step 4: Register operator ──
    await supabase_client.table("operator_whitelist").upsert({
        "telegram_id": operator_id,
        "name": "Primary Operator",
        "created_at": datetime.now(timezone.utc).isoformat(),
        "preferences": {"autonomy_mode": "autopilot", "execution_mode": "cloud"},
    }).execute()

    # ── Summary ──
    total = len(results["passed"]) + len(results["failed"]) + len(results["skipped"])
    await send_telegram_message(operator_id,
        f"📊 Setup Complete\n\n"
        f"✅ Passed: {len(results['passed'])}/{total}\n"
        f"❌ Failed: {len(results['failed'])}\n"
        f"⏭️ Skipped: {len(results['skipped'])}\n\n"
        f"{'Ready to build! Send /new' if not results['failed'] else 'Fix failed items and re-run /setup'}"
    )

    return results
```

**Wizard flow:** 8 API keys collected via Telegram → 5 service verifications → database initialization → operator registration → summary report.

**Key behaviors:**
- Each key has a 300-second entry timeout with SKIP default
- Keys are stored in GCP Secret Manager immediately upon receipt (never in env vars or config files)
- Verification failures are non-blocking — the wizard continues and reports all results at the end
- Database initialization only runs if the corresponding service verification passed

---

## §7.1.3 Database Schema Initialization

### Supabase Tables

```python
async def initialize_supabase_schema():
    """Create all required Supabase tables."""
    schemas = [
        # From Part 2 — Pipeline State
        """CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS pipeline_states (
            project_id TEXT PRIMARY KEY,
            operator_id TEXT NOT NULL,
            current_stage TEXT,
            state_json JSONB NOT NULL,
            snapshot_id INTEGER,
            selected_stack TEXT,
            execution_mode TEXT DEFAULT 'cloud',
            created_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW(),
            updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW()
        )""",

        """CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS state_snapshots (
            id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
            project_id TEXT NOT NULL,
            snapshot_id INTEGER NOT NULL,
            stage TEXT NOT NULL,
            state_json JSONB NOT NULL,
            git_commit_hash TEXT,
            created_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW(),
            UNIQUE(project_id, snapshot_id)
        )""",

        # From Part 5 — Operator Management
        """CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS operator_whitelist (
            telegram_id TEXT PRIMARY KEY,
            name TEXT,
            invite_code TEXT,
            created_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW(),
            preferences JSONB DEFAULT '{}'
        )""",

        """CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS operator_state (
            telegram_id TEXT PRIMARY KEY,
            state TEXT,
            context JSONB DEFAULT '{}',
            updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW()
        )""",

        """CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS active_projects (
            operator_id TEXT PRIMARY KEY,
            project_id TEXT NOT NULL,
            current_stage TEXT,
            state_json JSONB NOT NULL,
            started_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW(),
            updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW()
        )""",

        """CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS archived_projects (
            id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
            project_id TEXT UNIQUE,
            operator_id TEXT,
            final_stage TEXT,
            total_cost_usd REAL,
            state_json JSONB NOT NULL,
            archived_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW()
        )""",

        """CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS monthly_costs (
            id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
            operator_id TEXT,
            month TEXT,
            project_count INT DEFAULT 0,
            ai_total_usd REAL DEFAULT 0,
            infra_total_usd REAL DEFAULT 0,
            UNIQUE(operator_id, month)
        )""",

        """CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS memory_stats (
            id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
            stats JSONB NOT NULL,
            collected_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW()
        )""",
    ]

    for sql in schemas:
        await supabase_client.rpc("exec_sql", {"query": sql}).execute()
```

**8 tables total:** `pipeline_states`, `state_snapshots`, `operator_whitelist`, `operator_state`, `active_projects`, `archived_projects`, `monthly_costs`, `memory_stats`.

### Neo4j Indexes and Constraints

```python
async def initialize_neo4j_schema():
    """Create indexes and constraints for Mother Memory."""
    indexes = [
        "CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS FOR (p:Project) ON (p.id)",
        "CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS FOR (c:Component) ON (c.id)",
        "CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS FOR (c:Component) ON (c.stack)",
        "CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS FOR (ep:ErrorPattern) ON (ep.id)",
        "CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS FOR (ep:ErrorPattern) ON (ep.stack)",
        "CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS FOR (sp:StackPattern) ON (sp.id)",
        "CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS FOR (sp:StackPattern) ON (sp.stack)",
        "CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS FOR (d:DesignDNA) ON (d.id)",
        "CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS FOR (d:DesignDNA) ON (d.category)",
        "CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS FOR (rd:RegulatoryDecision) ON (rd.id)",
        "CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS FOR (lt:LegalDocTemplate) ON (lt.id)",
        "CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS FOR (g:Graveyard) ON (g.id)",
        "CREATE CONSTRAINT IF NOT EXISTS FOR (p:Project) REQUIRE p.id IS UNIQUE",
    ]

    for idx in indexes:
        await neo4j_run(idx)
```

**12 indexes** covering all 8 node types (Project, Component, ErrorPattern, StackPattern, DesignDNA, RegulatoryDecision, LegalDocTemplate, Graveyard) plus **1 uniqueness constraint** on `Project.id`.

# §7.2 Local Mode Setup

## §7.2.0 One-Click Local Agent (v5.4.2 — H6)

For operators with zero terminal experience: download a single file, double-click, done. The one-click agent is a PyInstaller-bundled binary that includes Python, Uvicorn, Cloudflared, and the local agent server. No terminal, no pip, no PATH configuration required.

**Download options:**

| Platform | File |
|----------|------|
| macOS (Apple Silicon) | `factory-agent-macos-arm64.app` |
| macOS (Intel) | `factory-agent-macos-x64.app` |
| Linux (x64) | `factory-agent-linux-x64` |

**Usage:**
1. Double-click the downloaded file
2. On first run: a browser window opens for Cloudflare Tunnel login
3. Enter the tunnel token provided during pipeline setup
4. Green status icon = connected
5. Close the window to disconnect

### PyInstaller Build Spec

```python
# [H6] PyInstaller build spec for one-click agent
# Build command: pyinstaller factory_agent.spec

# factory_agent.spec
a = Analysis(
    ['local_agent_server.py'],
    pathex=['.'],
    binaries=[
        ('cloudflared', '.'),  # Bundle cloudflared binary
    ],
    hiddenimports=['uvicorn', 'fastapi', 'httpx'],
)
pyz = PYZ(a.pure)
exe = EXE(pyz, a.scripts, a.binaries, a.datas,
    name='factory-agent',
    console=False,           # No terminal window
    icon='factory-icon.icns',
)
app = BUNDLE(exe, name='Factory Agent.app',
    bundle_identifier='com.aifactory.localagent',
    info_plist={
        'LSUIElement': '1',  # Menu bar only, no Dock icon
        'CFBundleShortVersionString': '5.4.2',
    },
)
```

**[H6] Rollback:** If the binary has issues, the operator can fall back to manual setup (§7.2.1 below). Both paths produce the same local agent server listening on port 8765.

---

## §7.2.1 Manual Installation (Alternative)

```bash
#!/bin/bash
# factory_local_setup.sh — Run on operator's Mac/Linux machine

echo "🏭 AI Factory Local Agent Setup"
echo "================================"

# 1. Install dependencies
pip install fastapi uvicorn --user
echo "✅ FastAPI + Uvicorn installed"

# 2. Install Cloudflare Tunnel
# macOS:
brew install cloudflared
# Linux:
# curl -L https://github.com/cloudflare/cloudflared/releases/latest/download/cloudflared-linux-amd64 \
#   -o /usr/local/bin/cloudflared

# 3. Create tunnel (one-time)
cloudflared tunnel login
cloudflared tunnel create factory-agent
echo "✅ Tunnel created"

# 4. Configure tunnel
cat > ~/.cloudflared/config.yml << EOF
tunnel: factory-agent
credentials-file: ~/.cloudflared/factory-agent.json
ingress:
  - hostname: factory-agent.YOUR_DOMAIN.com
    service: http://localhost:8765
  - service: http_status:404
EOF
echo "✅ Tunnel configured"

# 5. Save factory agent
cat > ~/factory_agent.py << 'AGENT'
"""AI Factory Local Agent — 30-line FastAPI server."""
from fastapi import FastAPI, HTTPException
from pydantic import BaseModel
import subprocess, os

app = FastAPI()
WORKSPACE = os.path.expanduser("~/factory-workspace")
os.makedirs(WORKSPACE, exist_ok=True)

PROHIBITED = [
    "sudo", "su -", "pkexec", "doas",
    "chmod 777", "chmod +s", "chown root",
    "rm -rf /", "dd if=",
]

class ExecRequest(BaseModel):
    command: str
    timeout: int = 300

@app.get("/heartbeat")
def heartbeat():
    return {"status": "alive", "workspace": WORKSPACE}

@app.post("/execute")
def execute(req: ExecRequest):
    if any(p in req.command for p in PROHIBITED):
        raise HTTPException(403, f"Prohibited command pattern detected")
    result = subprocess.run(
        req.command, shell=True, capture_output=True, text=True,
        timeout=req.timeout, cwd=WORKSPACE
    )
    return {
        "stdout": result.stdout[-5000:],
        "stderr": result.stderr[-2000:],
        "exit_code": result.returncode,
    }

@app.post("/upload")
def upload(path: str, content: str):
    full = os.path.join(WORKSPACE, path)
    os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(full), exist_ok=True)
    with open(full, "w") as f:
        f.write(content)
    return {"written": full}
AGENT
echo "✅ Agent saved"

# 6. Start (in two terminals)
echo ""
echo "Now run in Terminal 1: cloudflared tunnel run factory-agent"
echo "And in Terminal 2: uvicorn factory_agent:app --port 8765"
echo ""
echo "The pipeline will auto-detect your machine via heartbeat."
```

**Local agent endpoints:**
- `GET /heartbeat` — returns alive status + workspace path
- `POST /execute` — runs shell commands (with prohibited pattern filtering, 5000-char stdout limit, 2000-char stderr limit)
- `POST /upload` — writes files to workspace directory

---

## §7.2.2 Heartbeat Monitor Integration

```python
class HeartbeatMonitor:
    """Monitors local agent availability. Runs as background coroutine."""

    def __init__(self, tunnel_url: str, state: PipelineState):
        self.tunnel_url = tunnel_url
        self.state = state
        self.consecutive_failures = 0
        self.max_failures = 3  # 90 seconds before failover

    async def ping(self) -> bool:
        try:
            async with httpx.AsyncClient(timeout=10) as client:
                resp = await client.get(f"{self.tunnel_url}/heartbeat")
                if resp.status_code == 200:
                    self.consecutive_failures = 0
                    self.state.local_heartbeat_alive = True
                    return True
        except Exception:
            pass

        self.consecutive_failures += 1
        if self.consecutive_failures >= self.max_failures:
            self.state.local_heartbeat_alive = False
            if self.state.execution_mode in (ExecutionMode.LOCAL, ExecutionMode.HYBRID):
                # Auto-failover to Cloud
                # v5.4.1 Patch 12A: Failover is a resume-from-last-checkpoint operation.
                # It does NOT transfer in-progress local state, partial builds,
                # or ephemeral memory. The Cloud Orchestrator reads the last persisted
                # snapshot and resumes from the last completed stage. The next build
                # step pulls fresh code from GitHub.
                self.state.execution_mode = ExecutionMode.CLOUD
                await notify_operator(
                    self.state, NotificationType.HEARTBEAT_LOST,
                    "⚠️ Local machine unreachable (90s). Auto-switched to Cloud.\n"
                    "⚠️ Failover resumes from last completed stage checkpoint, "
                    "not in-progress work.\n"
                    "Restart your local agent and use /mode local to switch back."
                )
        return False

    async def run(self):
        while True:
            await self.ping()
            await asyncio.sleep(30)
```

**Heartbeat behavior:**
- Pings every **30 seconds** with 10-second timeout
- **3 consecutive failures** (90 seconds) triggers auto-failover to Cloud mode
- **Failover = resume-from-last-checkpoint** — does NOT transfer in-progress local state, partial builds, or ephemeral memory
- Cloud Orchestrator reads the last persisted snapshot and resumes from the last completed stage
- Operator can switch back with `/mode local` after restarting their agent

---

# §7.3 Disaster Recovery & 3AM Crash Recovery Playbook (v5.4.2 — H1)

> **[H1] The "3AM Test":** Can an operator who's woken at 3AM diagnose and fix any pipeline failure using only this section, their phone (Telegram), and a laptop? Every scenario below has three columns: what the system detects automatically, what the system does without human input, and what the operator must do if auto-recovery fails.

---

## §7.3.0 Startup Health Checks (v5.4.2 — H1)

When the pipeline service starts (cold boot or crash restart), it runs these checks **before accepting any work:**

```python
async def startup_health_checks() -> dict[str, bool]:
    """[H1] 6-service health check at startup. ALL must pass before pipeline
    accepts work. If any critical service fails, pipeline enters DEGRADED mode
    and alerts operator."""
    checks = {}

    # 1. Supabase (CRITICAL — no state without it)
    try:
        await supabase_client.table("active_projects").select("count").limit(1).execute()
        checks["supabase"] = True
    except Exception:
        checks["supabase"] = False

    # 2. Neo4j (WARNING — can proceed without Mother Memory)
    try:
        await neo4j_run("RETURN 1 AS ok")
        checks["neo4j"] = True
    except Exception:
        checks["neo4j"] = False

    # 3. GitHub (WARNING — can buffer commits)
    try:
        async with httpx.AsyncClient() as c:
            r = await c.get("https://api.github.com/rate_limit",
                headers={"Authorization": f"token {GITHUB_TOKEN}"})
            checks["github"] = r.status_code == 200
    except Exception:
        checks["github"] = False

    # 4. Telegram (CRITICAL — no operator communication)
    try:
        me = await bot.get_me()
        checks["telegram"] = me is not None
    except Exception:
        checks["telegram"] = False

    # 5. Anthropic API (CRITICAL — no AI processing)
    try:
        async with httpx.AsyncClient() as c:
            r = await c.get("https://api.anthropic.com/v1/models",
                headers={
                    "x-api-key": ANTHROPIC_API_KEY,
                    "anthropic-version": "2023-06-01",
                })
            checks["anthropic"] = r.status_code == 200
    except Exception:
        checks["anthropic"] = False

    # 6. Perplexity (WARNING — C5 degradation policy handles absence)
    try:
        async with httpx.AsyncClient() as c:
            r = await c.post("https://api.perplexity.ai/chat/completions",
                headers={"Authorization": f"Bearer {PERPLEXITY_KEY}"},
                json={"model": "sonar", "messages": [{"role": "user", "content": "ping"}]})
            checks["perplexity"] = r.status_code == 200
    except Exception:
        checks["perplexity"] = False

    critical_services = ["supabase", "telegram", "anthropic"]
    all_critical_ok = all(checks.get(s, False) for s in critical_services)

    if not all_critical_ok:
        failed = [s for s in critical_services if not checks.get(s, False)]
        log.critical(f"[H1] CRITICAL services down: {failed}. Pipeline in DEGRADED mode.")
        # Alert operator if Telegram is up
        if checks.get("telegram"):
            await bot.send_message(OPERATOR_ID,
                f"🚨 Pipeline started in DEGRADED mode\n"
                f"Failed: {', '.join(failed)}\n"
                f"Passed: {', '.join(s for s, ok in checks.items() if ok)}\n"
                f"Pipeline will NOT accept new projects until critical services recover."
            )

    return checks
```

**Service criticality classification:**

| Service | Criticality | If Down |
|---------|------------|---------|
| Supabase | **CRITICAL** | No state persistence — pipeline cannot function |
| Telegram | **CRITICAL** | No operator communication — pipeline cannot function |
| Anthropic | **CRITICAL** | No AI processing — pipeline cannot function |
| Neo4j | WARNING | Can proceed without Mother Memory; backfill on reconnect |
| GitHub | WARNING | Can buffer commits; push batch on reconnect |
| Perplexity | WARNING | [C5] degradation policy handles absence (cached → operator → UNVERIFIED) |

If any **CRITICAL** service fails → pipeline enters **DEGRADED mode** and will NOT accept new projects until recovery.

---

## §7.3.0a Crash Loop Detection (v5.4.2 — H1)

```python
CRASH_LOG_KEY = "pipeline_crash_log"
CRASH_THRESHOLD = 3
CRASH_WINDOW_MINUTES = 10

async def record_crash_and_check_loop() -> bool:
    """[H1] Returns True if crash loop detected (>3 crashes in 10 min).
    If loop detected, pipeline enters SAFE MODE and stops restarting."""
    now = datetime.now(timezone.utc)

    # Load crash log from Supabase (survives container restarts)
    log_data = await supabase_client.table("system_state") \
        .select("value").eq("key", CRASH_LOG_KEY).execute()
    crashes = json.loads(log_data.data[0]["value"]) if log_data.data else []
    crashes.append(now.isoformat())

    # Keep only crashes within window
    cutoff = now - timedelta(minutes=CRASH_WINDOW_MINUTES)
    recent = [c for c in crashes if datetime.fromisoformat(c) > cutoff]

    # Persist updated log
    await supabase_client.table("system_state").upsert({
        "key": CRASH_LOG_KEY, "value": json.dumps(recent)
    }).execute()

    if len(recent) >= CRASH_THRESHOLD:
        await bot.send_message(OPERATOR_ID,
            f"🚨 CRASH LOOP DETECTED\n"
            f"{len(recent)} crashes in {CRASH_WINDOW_MINUTES} min\n"
            f"Pipeline entering SAFE MODE — will NOT restart automatically.\n\n"
            f"Action required:\n"
            f"1. Check logs: `gcloud logging read 'resource.type=cloud_run_revision'`\n"
            f"2. Fix root cause\n"
            f"3. Clear crash log: /admin clear_crash_log\n"
            f"4. Redeploy or restart manually"
        )
        return True  # Crash loop — don't restart

    return False
```

**Crash loop logic:** ≥3 crashes in 10 minutes → **SAFE MODE** (pipeline frozen, no automatic restarts). Crash log is persisted in Supabase `system_state` table so it survives container restarts. The operator must manually fix the root cause, clear the crash log via `/admin clear_crash_log`, and redeploy.

---

## §7.3.0b Secondary Health Scheduler (v5.4.2 — H1)

```yaml
# Cloud Scheduler: every 30 minutes → POST /health-deep
# Complements startup checks with ongoing monitoring
- name: deep-health-check
  schedule: "*/30 * * * *"
  httpTarget:
    uri: https://factory-bot-HASH.run.app/health-deep
    httpMethod: POST
```

When `/health-deep` fires, the pipeline re-runs `startup_health_checks()` and compares against the last known state. If a previously-healthy service goes down, it sends an **immediate alert**. If a previously-down service comes back, it sends an **all-clear**. This provides continuous monitoring between startup events.

---

## §7.3.1 Failure Scenarios & Recovery (v5.4.2 — H1 expanded)

| # | Scenario | Impact | Auto-Detection | Auto-Action | Operator Instruction (if auto fails) |
|---|----------|--------|----------------|-------------|--------------------------------------|
| 1 | **Supabase down** | No state persistence | HTTP 5xx on upsert | Retry 3× with backoff → buffer in-memory → flush on reconnect | Check status.supabase.com. If prolonged: wait. State is buffered in-memory for up to 30 min. |
| 2 | **Neo4j down** | No Mother Memory queries | Connection error | Skip memory queries → proceed without reusable patterns → backfill on reconnect | Optional. Pipeline continues. Check neo4j.com/cloud/status. |
| 3 | **GitHub down** | No code versioning | API 5xx | Buffer commits locally → push batch on reconnect | Pipeline continues building. Check githubstatus.com. |
| 4 | **Perplexity down** | No Scout research | API error | [C5] Cached sources → operator sources → UNVERIFIED | Send `/provide_sources` with docs or `/wait` to retry in 30min. |
| 5 | **Anthropic down** | No AI processing | API error, 529 | Full pipeline halt → notify operator → retry every 15min | Wait for status.anthropic.com recovery. No manual action possible. |
| 6 | **Telegram down** | No operator comms | Webhook failures | Log all decisions → auto-select defaults → batch summary on reconnect | Check t.me/s/telegram_status. Decisions auto-selected. |
| 7 | **MacinCloud down** | No iOS/GUI builds | SSH timeout | Queue GUI builds → switch non-GUI to GitHub Actions | If urgent: use local Xcode. Otherwise wait for MacinCloud recovery. |
| 8 | **Cloudflare down** | No Local Mode | Heartbeat failures | Failover to Cloud (automatic, 90s) | Local work lost from last checkpoint. Pipeline resumes in Cloud. |
| 9 | **GCP down** | No Cloud hosting | Health check failures | N/A (service itself is down) | Check status.cloud.google.com. Deploy to backup region or wait. |
| 10 | **Operator unresponsive** | Decisions stall | 1hr timeout | Auto-select recommended option + continue | Review decisions when available via `/history`. |
| 11 | **Pipeline crash loop** | Repeated restarts | [H1] >3 crashes in 10min | Enter SAFE MODE → stop restarting → alert | Check logs, fix root cause, `/admin clear_crash_log`, redeploy. |
| 12 | **Budget exhausted** | Phase costs > limit | Circuit breaker tripped | Pipeline pauses → Telegram alert with cost breakdown | `/authorize` to override, `/cancel` to stop, `/budget` to see status. |

---

## §7.3.2 Disaster Recovery Runbook (v5.5 — FIX-12)

This runbook distills the H1 recovery infrastructure into a 4-step operator-followable sequence for 3AM incidents. Same mechanisms as §7.3.0–§7.3.1, reformatted for actionability.

### Step 1 — DETECT

Cloud Scheduler fires `/health-deep` every 15 minutes (§7.3.0b). If the health check fails or a project is stale >30 minutes, proceed to Step 2.

**Manual detection:** Operator notices Telegram alerts stop, or `/admin status` shows unhealthy services.

### Step 2 — CLASSIFY (choose one path)

| Condition | Path | Auto-Action |
|-----------|------|-------------|
| Orchestrator healthy + project stale >30min | **Stuck Project** | Auto-restore to last snapshot, re-launch stage (§7.3.4) |
| Orchestrator unhealthy + <3 crashes in 10min | **Auto-Restart** | Cloud Run restarts container; `startup_health_checks()` runs 6 services in order: Supabase → Neo4j → GitHub → Telegram → Anthropic → Perplexity (§7.3.0) |
| Orchestrator unhealthy + ≥3 crashes in 10min | **SAFE MODE** | Stop restarting; alert operator; pipeline frozen until manual intervention (§7.3.0a) |

### Step 3 — SAFE MODE Recovery (Telegram-Native) [FIX-20]

If the pipeline has entered SAFE MODE (≥3 crashes in 10 minutes), automated recovery has failed. All recovery commands below are Telegram-native — **no GCP Console needed.**

```python
# [FIX-20] Telegram-native SAFE MODE recovery commands (ADR-050)
SAFE_MODE_COMMANDS = {
    "/admin logs": {
        "action": "Fetch last 50 Cloud Run log lines via Cloud Logging API",
        "output": "Formatted log excerpt sent to Telegram chat",
        "note": "Look for: API key expiry, service outage, code bug",
    },
    "/admin rotate_key <service>": {
        "action": "Rotate API key for <service> in Secret Manager, redeploy",
        "services": ["anthropic", "perplexity", "supabase", "neo4j", "github"],
        "note": "Triggers automatic container restart after key update",
    },
    "/admin wait_for_recovery": {
        "action": "Pause pipeline, retry health checks every 5min for 1 hour",
        "output": "Telegram notification when service recovers or timeout reached",
        "note": "Best for external service outages (Anthropic, Supabase, etc.)",
    },
    "/admin support": {
        "action": "Generate diagnostic bundle (logs + state + health) for support ticket",
        "output": "Downloadable ZIP sent to Telegram",
        "note": "Use when root cause is unclear after /admin logs",
    },
}
```

**Recovery sequence (all via Telegram):**

1. **Check health:** `/admin status` — shows which of 6 services are healthy/unhealthy
2. **Read logs:** `/admin logs` — shows last 50 log lines (no GCP Console needed)
3. **Identify cause:**
   - API key expired → `/admin rotate_key <service>` (auto-redeploys)
   - Service outage → `/admin wait_for_recovery` (auto-retries for 1hr)
   - Unknown cause → `/admin support` (generates diagnostic bundle)
4. **Clear SAFE MODE:** `/admin clear_crash_log` — resets crash counter
5. **Auto-restart:** Orchestrator restarts with full `startup_health_checks()` sequence
6. **Verify:** Watch for "✅ All health checks passed" Telegram confirmation (<60s)

### §7.3.2a SAFE MODE Recovery — Advanced (GCP Console)

For operators comfortable with GCP Console, these advanced steps provide deeper diagnostics:

1. **Cloud Run logs:** GCP Console → Cloud Run → factory-bot → Logs tab → filter by severity=ERROR
2. **Secret Manager:** GCP Console → Secret Manager → verify key versions match expected
3. **Manual redeploy:** `gcloud run deploy factory-bot --image gcr.io/PROJECT_ID/factory-bot:latest --region me-central1`
4. **Force container restart:** `gcloud run services update factory-bot --region me-central1 --clear-env-vars && gcloud run services update factory-bot --region me-central1 --set-env-vars="RESTART_TRIGGER=$(date +%s)"`

**Note:** All advanced steps are optional. The Telegram-native commands in Step 3 are sufficient for all common failure scenarios.

### Step 4 — POST-INCIDENT

After recovery (whether automatic or manual), verify these three items:

1. **In-flight projects:** `/admin status` → confirm all active projects show "RUNNING" or "WAITING" (not "STALE" or "ERROR"). Any stuck projects should auto-resume within one Janitor cycle (6 hours) or can be manually resumed with `/continue`.

2. **Knowledge graph integrity:** The Janitor Agent runs every 6 hours and will detect/repair orphaned Neo4j nodes. If immediate verification is needed: check Mother Memory for nodes with `_hidden=true` that shouldn't be hidden.

3. **Audit trail:** Review the audit log (`/admin audit_log`) for any auto-selected decisions made during the outage (Scenario #6 and #10 in §7.3.1). Override any incorrect auto-selections with `/restore` if needed.

> **[FIX-12] Note:** This runbook is a reformatted view of the automated recovery infrastructure in §7.3.0–§7.3.1. The underlying mechanisms are identical. The runbook format is optimized for a sleep-deprived operator at 3AM.

---

## §7.3.3 Retry Logic

```python
import asyncio
from functools import wraps

def with_retry(max_retries=3, backoff_base=2, retryable_exceptions=(Exception,)):
    """Decorator for retryable operations with exponential backoff."""
    def decorator(fn):
        @wraps(fn)
        async def wrapper(*args, **kwargs):
            last_error = None
            for attempt in range(max_retries):
                try:
                    return await fn(*args, **kwargs)
                except retryable_exceptions as e:
                    last_error = e
                    wait = backoff_base ** attempt
                    await asyncio.sleep(wait)
            raise last_error
        return wrapper
    return decorator

# Applied to critical operations
@with_retry(max_retries=3, backoff_base=2)
async def persist_state_resilient(state: PipelineState):
    await persist_state(state)

@with_retry(max_retries=2, backoff_base=5)
async def github_commit_resilient(repo, path, content, message):
    await github_commit_file(repo, path, content, message)
```

**Retry configuration:**
- `persist_state`: 3 retries, 2-second exponential backoff (waits 1s, 2s, 4s)
- `github_commit`: 2 retries, 5-second exponential backoff (waits 1s, 5s)
- All retries use exponential backoff: `backoff_base ** attempt`

---

## §7.3.4 State Recovery on Restart

```python
async def recover_on_startup():
    """
    Called when the pipeline service restarts.
    Recovers any in-progress projects.
    """
    # Find active projects that may have been interrupted
    active = await supabase_client.table("active_projects").select("*").execute()

    for project in active.data:
        state = PipelineState.model_validate(project["state_json"])

        # Repair any snapshot gaps
        repaired = await repair_missing_snapshots(state.project_id)
        if repaired:
            await notify_operator(state, NotificationType.ERROR,
                f"🔧 Repaired {repaired} missing snapshots after restart.")

        # Check if project was mid-stage
        if state.current_stage not in (Stage.HALTED, Stage.COMPLETED):
            # Restore to last completed snapshot
            last_snap = await supabase_client.table("state_snapshots") \
                .select("snapshot_id, stage") \
                .eq("project_id", state.project_id) \
                .order("snapshot_id", desc=True).limit(1).execute()

            if last_snap.data:
                await notify_operator(state, NotificationType.ERROR,
                    f"🔄 Service restarted. Recovering {state.project_id} "
                    f"from snapshot #{last_snap.data[0]['snapshot_id']} "
                    f"({last_snap.data[0]['stage']}).\n"
                    f"Use /continue to resume or /restore to pick a different point."
                )
```

**Recovery flow on restart:**
1. Query all active projects from Supabase
2. For each project: repair any snapshot gaps (from §6.7 `repair_missing_snapshots`)
3. If project was mid-stage (not HALTED or COMPLETED): find last completed snapshot
4. Notify operator with recovery point and options (`/continue` or `/restore`)

---

## §7.3.5 Stuck Project Detection & Auto-Recovery (v5.4.1 Patch 6)

A Cloud Scheduler job `stuck-project-check` runs every 15 minutes to detect and recover crashed pipelines.

```python
# Cloud Scheduler: every 15 minutes → POST /janitor {"task": "stuck_check"}

async def detect_and_recover_stuck_projects():
    """
    Detect projects that stopped updating (pipeline crash mid-stage).
    Query: active_projects WHERE updated_at < NOW() - 30 minutes
           AND current_stage NOT IN ('S8_HANDOFF', 'HALTED', 'COMPLETED')
    """
    cutoff = datetime.now(timezone.utc) - timedelta(minutes=30)
    stuck = await supabase_client.table("active_projects") \
        .select("*") \
        .lt("updated_at", cutoff.isoformat()) \
        .not_.in_("current_stage", ["S8_HANDOFF", "HALTED", "COMPLETED"]) \
        .execute()

    for project in stuck.data:
        state = PipelineState.model_validate(project["state_json"])

        # 1. Read last successful snapshot
        last_snap = await supabase_client.table("state_snapshots") \
            .select("*").eq("project_id", state.project_id) \
            .neq("stage", "INVALID") \
            .order("snapshot_id", desc=True).limit(1).execute()

        if not last_snap.data:
            continue  # No recoverable snapshot

        snap = last_snap.data[0]

        # 2. Determine recovery point (last COMPLETED stage, not the failed one)
        recovery_stage = snap["stage"]

        # 3. Alert operator
        await notify_operator(state.operator_id, NotificationType.ERROR,
            f"⚠️ **Stuck Project Detected**\n"
            f"Project: {state.project_id}\n"
            f"Stuck at: {state.current_stage.value}\n"
            f"Last good snapshot: #{snap['snapshot_id']} ({recovery_stage})\n"
            f"Stale for: {int((datetime.now(timezone.utc) - datetime.fromisoformat(project['updated_at'])).total_seconds() / 60)} min\n\n"
            f"Auto-resuming from {recovery_stage}..."
        )

        # 4. Set recovering status
        await supabase_client.table("active_projects").update({
            "current_stage": "RECOVERING",
        }).eq("project_id", state.project_id).execute()

        # 5. Restore to last good snapshot and re-enqueue
        recovered_state = await restore_state(state.project_id, snap["snapshot_id"])

        # 6. Re-launch pipeline from recovered stage
        graph = build_pipeline_graph()
        asyncio.create_task(graph.ainvoke(recovered_state))

        # 7. Audit
        await audit_log("system", "stuck_project_recovered", {
            "project_id": state.project_id,
            "stuck_stage": state.current_stage.value,
            "recovered_to_snapshot": snap["snapshot_id"],
            "recovered_stage": recovery_stage,
        })
```

**Stuck detection criteria:** `updated_at` older than 30 minutes AND stage not in terminal states (S8_HANDOFF, HALTED, COMPLETED).

**Auto-recovery sequence:** Detect → alert operator → set RECOVERING status → restore to last good snapshot → re-launch pipeline → audit log entry.

### Cloud Run Probes (v5.4.1 Patch 6)

```yaml
# In Cloud Run service definition
spec:
  template:
    spec:
      containers:
        - image: gcr.io/PROJECT/factory-bot
          startupProbe:
            httpGet:
              path: /health
              port: 8080
            failureThreshold: 3
            periodSeconds: 10
          livenessProbe:
            httpGet:
              path: /health
              port: 8080
            periodSeconds: 30
          containerConcurrency: 1
          timeoutSeconds: 3600
```

### Stage Idempotency Guarantee (v5.4.1 Patch 6)

All stages S0–S8 are designed to be **idempotent**: re-running a stage from its beginning with the same inputs produces the same outputs without side effects. If a stage cannot be made fully idempotent (e.g., an external API call that already succeeded), the stage must check for prior completion before re-executing.

| Stage | Idempotency | Strategy |
|-------|-------------|----------|
| S0–S2 (analysis) | **Fully idempotent** | Regenerating intake/legal/blueprint from same inputs is safe |
| S3 (CodeGen) | **Idempotent** | Regenerated code overwrites previous version in Git |
| S4 (Build) | **Near-idempotent** | Build commands are repeatable; stale artifacts are cleaned first |
| S5 (Test) | **Fully idempotent** | Tests can be re-run safely |
| S6 (Deploy) | **Check-before-execute** | Before uploading, check if binary already exists on platform; skip upload if hash matches |
| S7 (Verify) | **Fully idempotent** | Health checks are read-only |
| S8 (Handoff) | **Check-before-execute** | Before generating docs, check if they already exist in `state.legal_documents` |

# §7.4 Monitoring

## §7.4.1 Health Endpoints

```python
# Cloud Run health check endpoints

async def health_check(request):
    """Basic liveness check."""
    return {"status": "ok", "version": "5.6"}

async def readiness_check(request):
    """Deep readiness: verify all dependencies."""
    checks = {}

    try:
        await supabase_client.table("operator_whitelist").select("count").limit(1).execute()
        checks["supabase"] = "ok"
    except:
        checks["supabase"] = "error"

    try:
        await neo4j_run("RETURN 1")
        checks["neo4j"] = "ok"
    except:
        checks["neo4j"] = "error"

    try:
        async with httpx.AsyncClient(timeout=5) as c:
            r = await c.get("https://api.anthropic.com/v1/models",
                headers={"x-api-key": await get_secret("ANTHROPIC_API_KEY")})
            checks["anthropic"] = "ok" if r.status_code == 200 else "degraded"
    except:
        checks["anthropic"] = "error"

    all_ok = all(v == "ok" for v in checks.values())
    return {"status": "ready" if all_ok else "degraded", "checks": checks}
```

**Two endpoints:**
- `/health` — basic liveness (always returns `ok` if process is running)
- `/health-deep` (readiness) — verifies Supabase, Neo4j, Anthropic connectivity; returns per-service status

## §7.4.2 Cost Monitoring Alerts

```python
COST_ALERT_THRESHOLDS = {
    "per_project_warning": 8.00,      # Warn at $8 per project
    "per_project_critical": 15.00,    # Critical at $15
    "monthly_warning": 180.00,        # [C2] Warn at ~73% of baseline
    "monthly_critical": BUDGET_CONFIG["variable_monthly_4proj"]["macincloud_payg"]
        + sum(BUDGET_CONFIG["variable_monthly_4proj"].values()),
    # [C2] Critical at variable subtotal ($75.55)
    # Note: fixed costs are infra, not triggerable per-project
}

# [C2] All thresholds derived from BUDGET_CONFIG, never hardcoded.
MONTHLY_BASELINE = (
    sum(BUDGET_CONFIG["fixed_monthly"].values())
    + sum(BUDGET_CONFIG["variable_monthly_4proj"].values())
)

async def check_cost_alerts(state: PipelineState):
    """Check cost thresholds and alert operator."""
    cost = state.total_cost_usd
    if cost > COST_ALERT_THRESHOLDS["per_project_critical"]:
        await notify_operator(state, NotificationType.BUDGET_ALERT,
            f"🚨 Project cost CRITICAL: ${cost:.2f} "
            f"(>${COST_ALERT_THRESHOLDS['per_project_critical']})\n"
            f"Consider /cancel or reducing scope."
        )
    elif cost > COST_ALERT_THRESHOLDS["per_project_warning"]:
        await notify_operator(state, NotificationType.BUDGET_ALERT,
            f"⚠️ Project cost elevated: ${cost:.2f}"
        )

async def check_monthly_cost_alerts(operator_id: str):
    """Monthly cost check — runs after each project completes.
    [C2] Reads from BUDGET_CONFIG."""
    month = datetime.now().strftime("%Y-%m")
    monthly = await supabase_client.table("monthly_costs") \
        .select("*").eq("operator_id", operator_id).eq("month", month).execute()

    if monthly.data:
        total = monthly.data[0]["ai_total_usd"] + monthly.data[0]["infra_total_usd"]
        baseline = MONTHLY_BASELINE  # [C2] From BUDGET_CONFIG, not hardcoded
        if total > baseline * 0.85:
            await send_telegram_message(operator_id,
                f"📊 Monthly spend: ${total:.2f}/${baseline:.2f} budget\n"
                f"Remaining: ${baseline-total:.2f} "
                f"({(baseline-total)*BUDGET_CONFIG['fx_rate']:.2f} SAR)"
            )
```

**Alert thresholds (all derived from BUDGET_CONFIG [C2]):**
- Per-project warning: $8.00
- Per-project critical: $15.00
- Monthly warning: $180.00 (~73% of baseline)
- Monthly alert triggers at 85% of `MONTHLY_BASELINE`

# §7.5 File Delivery Functions (v5.4.2 — C3)

> **[C3]** Previously undefined. The Airlock code called `upload_to_temp_storage()` and `send_telegram_file()` but neither was defined. These are now fully specified using Supabase Storage (existing dependency — no new cost).

```python
import os
import hashlib
from pathlib import Path

# [C3] Configurable limits — not hardcoded
TELEGRAM_FILE_LIMIT_MB = int(os.getenv("TELEGRAM_FILE_LIMIT_MB", "50"))   # [V12] Verified: 50MB for bots
SOFT_FILE_LIMIT_MB = int(os.getenv("SOFT_FILE_LIMIT_MB", "200"))
ARTIFACT_TTL_HOURS = int(os.getenv("ARTIFACT_TTL_HOURS", "72"))

def compute_sha256(file_path: str) -> str:
    """Compute SHA-256 checksum for integrity verification."""
    sha = hashlib.sha256()
    with open(file_path, "rb") as f:
        for chunk in iter(lambda: f.read(8192), b""):
            sha.update(chunk)
    return sha.hexdigest()
```

### upload_to_temp_storage()

```python
async def upload_to_temp_storage(
    file_path: str,
    project_id: str,
    ttl_hours: int = ARTIFACT_TTL_HOURS
) -> str:
    """[C3] Upload binary to Supabase Storage, return signed URL.

    Provider: Supabase Storage (existing dependency — no new cost)
    Auth: Service key (SUPABASE_SERVICE_KEY env var)
    TTL: 72 hours default, cleaned by Janitor Agent
    Bucket: build-artifacts (auto-created if missing)
    Returns: Signed download URL with expiry
    """
    bucket = "build-artifacts"
    object_key = f"{project_id}/{Path(file_path).name}"

    # Upload via Supabase Storage API
    with open(file_path, "rb") as f:
        await supabase_client.storage.from_(bucket).upload(
            object_key, f,
            file_options={"content-type": "application/octet-stream"}
        )

    # Generate signed URL with TTL
    signed = await supabase_client.storage.from_(bucket).create_signed_url(
        object_key, expires_in=ttl_hours * 3600
    )

    # Record for Janitor cleanup
    await supabase_client.table("temp_artifacts").insert({
        "project_id": project_id,
        "object_key": object_key,
        "bucket": bucket,
        "expires_at": (datetime.now(timezone.utc) + timedelta(hours=ttl_hours)).isoformat(),
        "size_bytes": os.path.getsize(file_path),
    }).execute()

    return signed["signedURL"]
```

### send_telegram_file()

```python
async def send_telegram_file(
    operator_id: str,
    file_path: str,
    project_id: str = ""
) -> None:
    """[C3] Size-aware file delivery via Telegram.

    ≤50MB:  Direct upload via Telegram Bot API sendDocument
    >50MB:  Upload to Supabase Storage, send signed URL + checksum
    """
    size_mb = os.path.getsize(file_path) / (1024 * 1024)

    if size_mb <= TELEGRAM_FILE_LIMIT_MB:
        # Direct upload via Telegram Bot API sendDocument [V12]
        with open(file_path, "rb") as f:
            await bot.send_document(operator_id, f, filename=Path(file_path).name)

    elif size_mb <= SOFT_FILE_LIMIT_MB:
        # Upload to Supabase Storage, send link
        url = await upload_to_temp_storage(file_path, project_id)
        checksum = compute_sha256(file_path)
        await bot.send_message(
            operator_id,
            f"📦 Build artifact ready (too large for direct send):\n"
            f"Download: {url}\n"
            f"SHA-256: {checksum}\n"
            f"Size: {size_mb:.1f} MB\n"
            f"Expires: {ARTIFACT_TTL_HOURS} hours"
        )

    else:
        # Over soft limit — warn operator, still upload
        url = await upload_to_temp_storage(file_path, project_id)
        checksum = compute_sha256(file_path)
        await bot.send_message(
            operator_id,
            f"📦 Large build artifact ({size_mb:.1f} MB):\n"
            f"Download: {url}\n"
            f"SHA-256: {checksum}\n"
            f"Expires: {ARTIFACT_TTL_HOURS} hours\n"
            f"Warning: File exceeds {SOFT_FILE_LIMIT_MB}MB soft limit. "
            f"Consider optimizing build size."
        )
```

**Size routing logic:**
- **≤50MB:** Direct Telegram Bot API `sendDocument` [V12 verified limit]
- **50–200MB:** Supabase Storage signed URL + SHA-256 checksum
- **>200MB:** Same as above + soft limit warning

**Janitor integration [C3]:** The Janitor Agent runs a cleanup task every 6 hours: `DELETE FROM temp_artifacts WHERE expires_at < NOW()` followed by `supabase.storage.from_('build-artifacts').remove([object_key])` for each expired entry.

---

# §7.6 App Store Airlock (Binary Delivery Fallback) (v5.6 — H2+FIX-09+FIX-22)

```
┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  SCOPE DISCLAIMER (FIX-09)                                              │
│                                                                          │
│  The App Store Airlock is a compliance mitigation layer. It:            │
│  • Avoids prohibited automation (portal UI login, web scraping)         │
│  • Surfaces known policy risks via StorePolicyEvent queries (advisory)  │
│  • Generates compliance artifact templates (FIX-07)                     │
│  • Delivers build binaries when API uploads fail                        │
│                                                                          │
│  It does NOT guarantee that Apple or Google will approve any            │
│  submission. All Preflight checks and StorePolicyEvent usage are        │
│  classified as advisory. Ultimate compliance responsibility rests       │
│  with the operator. Store review policies change without notice and     │
│  are enforced at the discretion of Apple/Google reviewers.              │
└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

## §7.6.0 How It Actually Works (v5.4.2 — H2/M7)

**[M7] Concrete systems, not marketing:** The Airlock is the fallback delivery path when programmatic App Store / Play Store uploads fail. It packages the build binary, sends it to the operator via Telegram (using `send_telegram_file()` [C3] for ≤50MB or `upload_to_temp_storage()` for larger files), and provides step-by-step manual upload instructions. It does NOT attempt to bypass store review policies. It does NOT auto-submit on the operator's behalf. It is a file transfer mechanism with instructional guidance.

> **[FIX-22] Clarification:** The name "Airlock" may suggest a security quarantine. In this specification, Airlock refers exclusively to the **binary delivery fallback path** — when programmatic API uploads to App Store Connect or Google Play Console fail, the Airlock packages the compiled binary and delivers it to the operator via Telegram for manual submission. Think of it as "the airlock between automated builds and manual store uploads."

### §7.6.0a Automation vs Manual Boundaries (v5.4.2 — H2)

| Step | Automated? | What the pipeline does | What the operator must do |
|------|-----------|------------------------|---------------------------|
| Build binary (.ipa / .aab) | **Yes** | S4 Build stage compiles via Xcode/Gradle | Nothing |
| Code sign (iOS) | **Yes** | Fastlane match with provisioning profiles | Must have valid Apple Dev membership |
| Upload to App Store Connect | **Attempted** | Uses Transporter CLI or App Store Connect API | If API fails → Airlock delivers binary |
| Upload to Play Console | **Attempted** | Uses Google Play Developer API | If API fails → Airlock delivers binary |
| Store policy compliance | **Advisory** | Preflight check at S1 (see below) | Operator makes final submission decision |
| Store review response | **No** | Cannot respond to Apple/Google reviewer | Operator handles review feedback |

### §7.6.0b STRICT_STORE_COMPLIANCE Flag (v5.4.2 — H2)

```python
# [H2] Controls whether store compliance gate is advisory or blocking.
# Default: False (advisory) — logs warnings but doesn't block pipeline.
# Set True for production deployments where store rejection is costly.
STRICT_STORE_COMPLIANCE = os.getenv("STRICT_STORE_COMPLIANCE", "false").lower() == "true"

class ComplianceGateResult(BaseModel):
    """[H2] Structured output from S1 App Store compliance preflight."""
    platform: str              # "ios" | "android" | "both"
    overall_pass: bool         # True if no blockers found
    blockers: list[dict] = Field(default_factory=list)
        # [{guideline, section, risk, suggestion}]
    warnings: list[dict] = Field(default_factory=list)
        # [{guideline, section, risk, suggestion}]
    guidelines_version: str = ""   # e.g., "Apple HIG 2025-Q4", "Play Policy 2025-12-01"
    confidence: float = 0.0        # 0.0–1.0 — how confident the LLM is
    source_ids: list[str] = Field(default_factory=list)
        # [C5] Traceability to web-grounded sources

    def should_block(self) -> bool:
        """Block only if STRICT mode AND blockers found AND confidence > 0.7"""
        return STRICT_STORE_COMPLIANCE and len(self.blockers) > 0 and self.confidence > 0.7
```

**[H2/FIX-09] Policy:** The preflight compliance gate uses `StorePolicyEvent` nodes in Neo4j to track past rejections and learn from them. All Preflight checks and StorePolicyEvent queries are **advisory** — they surface risks, they do not determine compliance.

- If `STRICT_STORE_COMPLIANCE=false` (default): blockers are logged as warnings and the pipeline continues.
- If `true`: the pipeline halts and requires operator `/force_continue` [FIX-06].
- In either mode, the LLM's interpretation of store guidelines is advisory only — it cannot definitively determine whether Apple or Google will approve a submission.

---

## §7.6.1 Problem

App Store and Play Store uploads sometimes fail via API due to: code signing issues, provisioning profile expiration, API rate limits, or policy changes. The pipeline must not halt on deployment failures.

## §7.6.2 Solution: Binary Telegram Delivery

```python
async def airlock_deliver(
    state: PipelineState,
    platform: str,
    binary_path: str,
    error: str,
) -> dict:
    """
    When API upload fails, deliver binary directly to operator via Telegram.
    Operator drag-and-drops to App Store Connect / Play Console.
    """
    # Determine file type
    extensions = {"ios": ".ipa", "android": ".aab"}
    ext = extensions.get(platform, ".bin")

    # Check file size (Telegram limit: 50MB)
    size_mb = os.path.getsize(binary_path) / (1024 * 1024)

    if size_mb > 50:
        # Too large for Telegram — use C3 upload_to_temp_storage()
        upload_url = await upload_to_temp_storage(binary_path, state.project_id)  # [C3]
        await send_telegram_message(state.operator_id,
            f"📦 {platform.upper()} binary too large for Telegram ({size_mb:.1f} MB)\n"
            f"Download: {upload_url}\n"
            f"Link expires in 24 hours.\n\n"
            f"Upload to {'App Store Connect' if platform == 'ios' else 'Play Console'} manually."
        )
        return {"method": "temp_storage", "url": upload_url}

    # Send via Telegram
    await send_telegram_message(state.operator_id,
        f"🔒 {platform.upper()} Airlock\n\n"
        f"API upload failed: {error[:200]}\n\n"
        f"Sending you the {ext} file. Upload manually to "
        f"{'App Store Connect (Transporter app or web)' if platform == 'ios' else 'Play Console (Production > Releases)'}."
    )
    await send_telegram_file(state.operator_id, binary_path, state.project_id)  # [C3]

    # Also send upload instructions
    if platform == "ios":
        await send_telegram_message(state.operator_id,
            "📋 iOS Upload Steps:\n"
            "1. Open Transporter app (macOS)\n"
            "2. Drag the .ipa file into Transporter\n"
            "3. Click 'Deliver'\n"
            "4. Go to App Store Connect > TestFlight to verify"
        )
    else:
        await send_telegram_message(state.operator_id,
            "📋 Android Upload Steps:\n"
            "1. Open Play Console > your app\n"
            "2. Go to Release > Production (or Testing)\n"
            "3. Create new release\n"
            "4. Upload the .aab file\n"
            "5. Review and roll out"
        )

    return {"method": "telegram", "size_mb": size_mb}
```

**v5.4.1 Patch 7 — Policy vs. Access Disclaimer:**

The Airlock protects against **API/tooling failures** and operator access issues. It does NOT protect against content policy violations, guideline changes, or account-level enforcement actions. For policy resilience, see the Preflight Compliance Gate (§4.2, Step 5).

The `airlock_deliver` function appends this warning to every Telegram delivery:

> ⚠️ IMPORTANT: Manual upload does not bypass Apple/Google review. Your app may still be rejected for policy violations. Review compliance warnings from S1 Legal Gate before submitting.

---

# §7.7 Security Hardening

## §7.7.1 Secret Management

```python
# All secrets stored in GCP Secret Manager (not env vars, not config files)

async def get_secret(name: str) -> str:
    """Retrieve secret from GCP Secret Manager."""
    from google.cloud import secretmanager
    client = secretmanager.SecretManagerServiceAsyncClient()
    response = await client.access_secret_version(
        name=f"projects/{GCP_PROJECT_ID}/secrets/{name}/versions/latest"
    )
    return response.payload.data.decode("utf-8")

async def store_secret(name: str, value: str):
    """Store or update secret in GCP Secret Manager."""
    from google.cloud import secretmanager
    client = secretmanager.SecretManagerServiceAsyncClient()
    parent = f"projects/{GCP_PROJECT_ID}"
    try:
        await client.create_secret(
            parent=parent,
            secret_id=name,
            secret={"replication": {"automatic": {}}},
        )
    except Exception:
        pass  # Secret already exists
    await client.add_secret_version(
        parent=f"{parent}/secrets/{name}",
        payload={"data": value.encode("utf-8")},
    )
```

### Required Secrets

```python
REQUIRED_SECRETS = [
    "ANTHROPIC_API_KEY", "PERPLEXITY_API_KEY",
    "SUPABASE_URL", "SUPABASE_SERVICE_KEY",
    "NEO4J_URI", "NEO4J_PASSWORD",
    "GITHUB_TOKEN", "TELEGRAM_BOT_TOKEN",
    "GCP_PROJECT_ID",
    # Conditional
    "APPLE_API_KEY_ID", "APPLE_API_ISSUER_ID",
    "FLUTTERFLOW_API_TOKEN",
    "FIREBASE_SERVICE_ACCOUNT",
]
```

**9 required secrets + 4 conditional** — all stored in GCP Secret Manager with automatic replication. No secrets in env vars, config files, or hardcoded values.

## §7.7.2 User-Space Enforcer (Complete)

```python
PROHIBITED_PATTERNS = [
    "sudo ", "su -", "pkexec", "doas ",
    "chmod 777", "chmod +s", "chown root",
    "/usr/sbin/", "rm -rf /", "dd if=",
    "curl | sh", "curl | bash", "wget | sh",
    "mkfs", "fdisk", "mount ", "umount ",
    "> /dev/", "systemctl", "service ",
]

SAFE_REWRITES = {
    "pip install ": "pip install --user ",
    "pip3 install ": "pip3 install --user ",
    "npm install -g ": "npx ",
}

def enforce_user_space(command: str) -> str:
    """
    Validate and sanitize every command before execution.
    Raises UserSpaceViolation for prohibited patterns.
    Applies safe rewrites for common patterns.
    """
    # Check prohibited
    for pattern in PROHIBITED_PATTERNS:
        if pattern in command:
            raise UserSpaceViolation(
                f"Prohibited command pattern: '{pattern}' in command: {command[:100]}"
            )
    # Apply safe rewrites
    for old, new in SAFE_REWRITES.items():
        if old in command and new not in command:
            command = command.replace(old, new)
    return command

class UserSpaceViolation(Exception):
    pass
```

**Zero-sudo guarantee:** Every command generated by AI or executed by the pipeline passes through `enforce_user_space()` before execution.

**16 prohibited patterns:** sudo, su, pkexec, doas, chmod 777, chmod +s, chown root, /usr/sbin/, rm -rf /, dd if=, curl pipe to shell, mkfs, fdisk, mount/umount, /dev/ writes, systemctl/service.

**3 safe rewrites:** pip install → pip install --user; pip3 install → pip3 install --user; npm install -g → npx.

---

## §7.7.3 API Key Rotation

```python
async def rotate_api_keys():
    """
    Quarterly reminder to rotate API keys.
    Triggered by Cloud Scheduler.
    """
    operators = await supabase_client.table("operator_whitelist") \
        .select("telegram_id").execute()

    for op in operators.data:
        await send_telegram_message(op["telegram_id"],
            "🔐 Quarterly Security Reminder\n\n"
            "Please rotate these API keys:\n"
            "• Anthropic API key\n"
            "• Perplexity API key\n"
            "• GitHub token\n"
            "• Supabase service key\n\n"
            "Run /setup to update keys."
        )
```

**Cadence:** Quarterly via Cloud Scheduler. Notification-only — operator performs rotation manually and re-runs `/setup` to update stored secrets.

# §7.8 Deployment Architecture

## §7.8.1 Cloud Run Services

```yaml
# service: factory-bot (Telegram webhook + pipeline orchestrator)
# Memory: 1 GiB, CPU: 1, Min instances: 1 (always-on for webhooks)
# Max instances: 3 (auto-scale for concurrent projects)
# Timeout: 3600s (1 hour max per request)
# Region: me-central1 (Saudi Arabia)

apiVersion: serving.knative.dev/v1
kind: Service
metadata:
  name: factory-bot
spec:
  template:
    metadata:
      annotations:
        autoscaling.knative.dev/minScale: "1"
        autoscaling.knative.dev/maxScale: "3"
    spec:
      containerConcurrency: 10
      timeoutSeconds: 3600
      containers:
        - image: gcr.io/PROJECT_ID/factory-bot:latest
          resources:
            limits:
              memory: 1Gi
              cpu: "1"
          # [FIX-18] Startup probe — orchestrator supervisor (Level 1)
          # Cloud Run restarts container on failure
          # (max 3 attempts matches §7.3.0a crash-loop threshold)
          startupProbe:
            httpGet:
              path: /health
              port: 8080
            initialDelaySeconds: 5
            periodSeconds: 10
            failureThreshold: 3   # 3 failures = container marked unhealthy → restart
          livenessProbe:
            httpGet:
              path: /health
              port: 8080
            periodSeconds: 30
            failureThreshold: 3
          env:
            - name: GCP_PROJECT_ID
              value: PROJECT_ID
```

### [FIX-18] External Supervisor — GCP Uptime Check

```python
# [FIX-18] External supervisor: GCP Uptime Check monitors the orchestrator itself
# If Cloud Run service is unreachable for >5 minutes, alert via Telegram webhook
# This is the "supervisor of the supervisor" — answers "who watches the watchmen?"

UPTIME_CHECK_CONFIG = {
    "display_name": "factory-bot-health",
    "monitored_resource": "cloud_run_revision",
    "http_check": {
        "path": "/health",
        "port": 443,
        "use_ssl": True,
    },
    "period": "300s",     # Every 5 minutes
    "timeout": "10s",
    "alert_policy": {
        "conditions": [{"threshold": {"duration": "300s"}}],   # Alert after 5min downtime
        "notification_channels": ["telegram_webhook"],          # Routes to operator Telegram
    },
}
```

### [FIX-18] Supervision Chain

| Level | Supervisor | Action |
|-------|-----------|--------|
| **Level 0** | Pipeline code | Self-healing (startup_health_checks, crash-loop detection) |
| **Level 1** | Cloud Run | Restarts container (max 3 attempts, startupProbe) |
| **Level 2** | GCP Uptime Check | Alerts operator if Cloud Run itself is down |
| **Level 3** | Operator | Manual redeployment via GCP Console or `gcloud run deploy` |

---

## §7.8.2 Cloud Scheduler Jobs

```yaml
jobs:
  - name: janitor-clean
    schedule: "0 */6 * * *"       # Every 6 hours
    target: factory-bot/janitor
    body: '{"task": "janitor_clean"}'

  - name: snapshot-prune
    schedule: "0 0 1 * *"         # 1st of month
    target: factory-bot/janitor
    body: '{"task": "snapshot_prune"}'

  - name: memory-stats
    schedule: "0 0 * * *"         # Daily
    target: factory-bot/janitor
    body: '{"task": "memory_stats"}'

  - name: key-rotation-reminder
    schedule: "0 0 1 */3 *"       # Quarterly
    target: factory-bot/janitor
    body: '{"task": "key_rotation"}'
```

**4 scheduled jobs:** janitor cleanup (6h), snapshot pruning (monthly), memory stats (daily), key rotation reminder (quarterly). All within GCP Cloud Scheduler free tier (3 free jobs — the 4th is negligible cost).

# §7.11 ADR Supplement (Parts 2–7)

| ADR | Decision | Rationale |
|-----|----------|-----------|
| ADR-018 | Perplexity Sonar as sole web research agent | Grounded answers with citations, cheaper than Opus for research |
| ADR-019 | Sonar auto-select (standard vs pro) | Pro triggers on legal/debugging keywords, saves cost on simple lookups |
| ADR-020 | Strategist call limits per context | Opus at $5/$25/M must be rationed; fallback to Sonnet for non-critical |
| ADR-021 | 3 visual mocks to Telegram at S2 | Operator sees design before code is written; reduces rework |
| ADR-022 | Grid Enforcer as Pydantic validators | 4px grid + WCAG AA enforced at model level, not just AI prompt |
| ADR-023 | DocuGen bilingual Arabic+English | KSA market requires both languages for legal docs |
| ADR-024 | 4-way decision matrix (never open-ended) | Reduces operator cognitive load, enables timeout auto-selection |
| ADR-025 | Async decision queue with 1hr timeout | Pipeline never blocks indefinitely on operator response |
| ADR-026 | Notification filter by autonomy mode | Autopilot reduces noise; Copilot provides full visibility |
| ADR-027 | Bidirectional time travel | Forward restore prevents data loss on accidental rollback |
| ADR-028 | Delta Engine for restore previews | Operator sees what they'll lose/gain before committing to restore |
| ADR-029 | 5-tier snapshot retention | Balances storage cost with restore capability over time |
| ADR-030 | Mother Memory relabel (not delete) | Graveyard nodes recoverable; no permanent data loss |
| ADR-031 | Cross-project error learning | War Room skips L1 for errors seen 3+ times — faster fixes |
| ADR-032 | App Store Airlock via Telegram | Binary delivery ensures deployment never fully fails |
| ADR-033 | GCP Secret Manager for all secrets | No env vars, no config files, no hardcoded keys |
| ADR-034 | Cloud Run me-central1 region | Minimizes latency to KSA operators and services |

## 8.1  Production Readiness Scorecard

Every v5.4 capability is graded against three criteria:

- **Spec**: Is it fully specified with schemas, code, and contracts? (not "TBD")
- **Testable**: Can it be verified in isolation before full integration?
- **Budget**: Does it fit within the verified **$255.30/month** baseline (from `BUDGET_CONFIG`)?

| #  | Capability | Spec | Testable | Budget | Notes |
|----|-----------|------|----------|--------|-------|

| 3  | War Room L1→L2→L3 | ✅ | Inject errors, verify escalation | $0.05–$0.50/activation | Part 2 §2.3 |
| 4  | Stack Selector Brain | ✅ | Feed 6 requirement sets, verify correct stack | ~$0.03/selection | Part 2 §2.4 |
| 5  | Three-Mode Execution (Cloud/Local/Hybrid) | ✅ | Test each mode with mock executor | $0–$17/mo | Part 2 §2.5 |
| 6  | Heartbeat Monitor + Auto-Failover | ✅ | Kill local agent, verify failover | $0 | Part 2 §2.5 |
| 7  | Time-Travel Snapshots | ✅ | Persist→Restore→Verify state match | ~$0.001/snap | Part 2 §2.6 |
| 8  | Continuous Legal Thread | ✅ | Mock legal checks, verify halt behavior | ~$0.05/check | Part 2 §2.7 |

### 8.2.4  Budget Guardrails (Code-Enforced)

> v5.4.1 Patch 2: Per-role circuit breaker + Patch 4: corrected fixed costs

```python
BUDGET_GUARDRAILS = {
    # Per-role phase limits (v5.4.1 — replaces flat $2/phase)
    "phase_limits": {
        "scout_research":      2.00,
        "strategist_planning": 5.00,
        "design_engine":      10.00,
        "codegen_engineer":   25.00,
        "testing_qa":          8.00,
        "deploy_release":      5.00,
        "legal_guardian":      3.00,
        "war_room_debug":     15.00,
    },
    "per_project_cap_usd":     25.00,    # Hard cap per project
    "monthly_ai_hard_cap":     80.00,    # Hard stop for all AI calls
    "monthly_infra_expected": 202.50,    # Alert if >20% variance (v5.4.1: corrected)
    "macincloud_hours_cap":    20,       # Per month
    "strategist_calls_cap":     8,       # Per project (most expensive model)
}
```

```python
async def enforce_monthly_cap(state: PipelineState) -> bool:
    """Check if monthly AI spend has hit hard cap."""
    monthly = await get_monthly_cost_summary(state.operator_id)
    ai_total = monthly.get("ai_total", 0)

    if ai_total >= BUDGET_GUARDRAILS["monthly_ai_hard_cap"]:
        await send_telegram_message(
            state.operator_id,
            f"🛑 Monthly AI budget exhausted: ${ai_total:.2f} / "
            f"${BUDGET_GUARDRAILS['monthly_ai_hard_cap']:.2f}\n\n"
            f"No further AI calls until next month.\n"
            f"Contact admin to increase cap."
        )
        state.legal_halt = True
        state.legal_halt_reason = "Monthly AI budget cap reached"
        return False

    if ai_total >= BUDGET_GUARDRAILS["monthly_ai_hard_cap"] * 0.8:
        await send_telegram_message(
            state.operator_id,
            f"⚠️ Monthly AI budget at 80%: ${ai_total:.2f} / "
            f"${BUDGET_GUARDRAILS['monthly_ai_hard_cap']:.2f}"
        )
    return True
```


### 8.2.5  Additional & Variable Costs (v5.5 — updated)

The following costs are real but **not included in the $255.30 baseline** (`BUDGET_CONFIG`) because they are one-time or variable:

| Cost Item | Amount | Frequency | Notes |
|-----------|--------|-----------|-------|
| Apple Developer Program | $99.00 | Annual | [FIX-01] Now in BUDGET_CONFIG as $8.25/mo fixed |
| Google Play Developer Console | $25.00 | One-time | Required for Google Play publishing |
| Data egress (GCP + Firebase + Supabase) | $5–10 | Monthly est. | Negligible at 4 projects/mo; scales with media assets |
| MacinCloud hour overages | $0–15 | Monthly var. | [C9] Kill switch limits max session to 60min; overages from multiple sessions only |
| MacinCloud PAYG rounding | ~$1–3 | Monthly var. | [M1] Login time rounds up to nearest hour per calendar day [V10,V11] |
| Neo4j instance scaling | $0–35 | Monthly var. | If Mother Memory exceeds AuraDB Pro baseline |
| Claude long-context (>200K tokens) | $0–10 | Monthly rare | [M5] Only if projects require extended context; premium rates apply |
| Perplexity search fees | $2–8 | Monthly var. | [M3] Request fees per 1K queries at Medium context ($8–10/1K) |
| Perplexity Pro (optional) | $0–20 | Monthly opt. | $5 monthly API credit offsets token costs if subscribed |

**MacinCloud Clarification (v5.4.2 — C9):**

The $30/mo budget is a conservative estimate (~25-30 hours × $1/hour PAYG). Key billing rules [V10, V11]:

1. **PAYG blocks**: Prepaid 25-hour or 7-day credit blocks. Auto-refill when exhausted.
2. **Hourly rounding**: Login time is summed daily, then rounded UP to the nearest whole hour. A 10-minute build session costs 1 full hour ($1).
3. **Credit expiry**: Unused credits expire after 60 consecutive days without login [V11].
4. **Kill switch [C9]**: Every MacinCloud session starts with `shutdown -h +60` (OS-level 60-minute auto-shutdown). Cancelled on successful build completion. Prevents runaway billing from stuck sessions.

```python
# [C9] MacinCloud OS-Level Kill Switch
# Prevents runaway billing from stuck SSH sessions, zombie builds,
# or forgotten connections.

import subprocess

MACINCLOUD_SESSION_TIMEOUT_MIN = int(
    os.getenv("MACINCLOUD_SESSION_TIMEOUT_MIN", "60")
)

async def start_mac_session_safe(project_id: str, task: str) -> dict:
    """Start MacinCloud session with OS-level safety timer.

    1. SSH into Mac
    2. Immediately set shutdown timer (OS-level — survives process crash)
    3. Run build task
    4. Cancel shutdown on success
    5. Disconnect
    """
    ssh = await connect_macincloud()
    try:
        # [C9] Set OS-level kill switch FIRST — before any build work
        await ssh.run(f"sudo shutdown -h +{MACINCLOUD_SESSION_TIMEOUT_MIN}")
        log.info(
            f"[C9] Kill switch armed: "
            f"{MACINCLOUD_SESSION_TIMEOUT_MIN}min for {project_id}/{task}"
        )

        # Record session start for Janitor monitoring
        await supabase_client.table("mac_sessions").insert({
            "project_id":      project_id,
            "task":            task,
            "started_at":      datetime.now(timezone.utc).isoformat(),
            "timeout_minutes": MACINCLOUD_SESSION_TIMEOUT_MIN,
            "status":          "running",
        }).execute()

        # Execute the actual build task
        result = await execute_build_task(ssh, project_id, task)

        # [C9] Cancel shutdown on success
        await ssh.run("sudo shutdown -c")
        log.info(
            f"[C9] Kill switch disarmed: "
            f"{project_id}/{task} completed successfully"
        )

        # Update session record
        await supabase_client.table("mac_sessions").update({
            "status":       "completed",
            "completed_at": datetime.now(timezone.utc).isoformat(),
        }).eq("project_id", project_id).eq("status", "running").execute()

        return result

    except Exception as e:
        # Kill switch remains armed — Mac will shut down at timeout
        log.error(
            f"[C9] Mac session error for {project_id}: {e}. "
            f"Kill switch still armed."
        )
        await supabase_client.table("mac_sessions").update({
            "status": "error",
            "error":  str(e)[:500],
        }).eq("project_id", project_id).eq("status", "running").execute()
        raise
    finally:
        await ssh.close()
```

> **[C9] Janitor monitoring**: The Janitor Agent checks `mac_sessions` every 15 minutes. Any session with `status='running'` and `started_at` older than 90 minutes triggers an operator alert and forced session termination via MacinCloud API.


### 8.2.6  Scenario Cost Projections (v5.5 — M8+FIX-01+FIX-14)

| Projects/Month | Fixed Cost | Est. Variable | Est. Total USD | SAR Equivalent | Buffer vs $800 | Mitigations Needed |
|---------------|-----------|--------------|---------------|---------------|---------------|-------------------|
| 4 (baseline) | $179.75 | $75.55 | **$255.30** | 957 | **68.1%** | None — baseline operation |
| 8 | $179.75 | $151.10 | **$330.85** | 1,241 | **58.6%** | Monitor Perplexity search fees |
| 12 | $179.75 | $226.65 | **$406.40** | 1,524 | **49.2%** | Consider Batch API (50% off) |
| 20 | $179.75 | $377.75 | **$557.50** | 2,091 | **30.3%** | Batch API mandatory; reduce Opus calls; consider Neo4j Pro upgrade |
| 50 | $179.75 | $944.38 | **$1,124.13** | 4,215 | **OVER** | Exceeds $800 ceiling. Requires: (1) Raise ceiling to 5,000 SAR, (2) Batch API everywhere, (3) Haiku replaces Sonnet for simple codegen, (4) FlutterFlow Team plan if >1 operator |
| 100 | $179.75 | $1,888.75 | **$2,068.50** | 7,757 | **OVER** | [FIX-14] Enterprise tier. Requires: (1) Raise ceiling to 8,000+ SAR, (2) Batch API mandatory all stages, (3) Haiku for S0/S1/S5, Sonnet only for S3/S4, Opus only for L3 War Room, (4) Multiple Cloud Run instances (horizontal scaling), (5) Dedicated MacinCloud plan ($49+/mo), (6) Neo4j AuraDB Pro ($200+/mo), (7) Second operator + FlutterFlow Team, (8) Budget Governor [FIX-05] AMBER tier will activate automatically — plan for degraded model operation |

**[M8+FIX-14] Scaling decision tree:**

- **4–8 projects**: No changes needed. Baseline config handles this.
- **8–12 projects**: Enable Batch API for non-urgent stages (S3 CodeGen, S5 Test). Saves ~30% on AI.
- **12–20 projects**: Mandatory Batch API. Reduce Opus usage to L3 War Room only. Consider Haiku for S0/S1 analysis.
- **20–50 projects**: Raise SAR ceiling. Add second operator (FlutterFlow Team plan at $160/mo). Consider Neo4j scaling budget.
- **50–100 projects**: Enterprise tier. Multiple Cloud Run instances. Dedicated MacinCloud. Budget Governor [FIX-05] will activate AMBER/RED modes — plan for degraded model operation as a feature, not a bug.
- **100+ projects**: Full enterprise restructuring. Dedicated infrastructure, multi-operator fleet, custom SLAs with providers, Budget Governor ceiling raised to 8,000+ SAR. Variable cost dominates; optimize per-call cost ruthlessly.

Even at the high end of 12 projects/month ($406/mo = ~1,524 SAR), the system remains well within the 3,000 SAR ceiling with a 49% buffer.
